Utah Code Annotated - Title 9 - Cultural and Community Engagement
=================================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 9 - Chapter 1 - General Policies and Administration of the Department of Cultural and Community Engagement
**************************************************************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-101 Title.
------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-101(1): This title is known as "Cultural and Community Engagement."
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-101(2): This chapter is known as "General Policies and Administration of the Department of Cultural and Community Engagement."


Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-102 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this title:Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-102(1): "Department" means the Department of Cultural and Community Engagement.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-102(2): "Executive director" means the executive director of the Department of Cultural and Community Engagement.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-102(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-102(3)(a): "Pass-through funding" means funding from an appropriation by the Legislature to a state agency that is intended to be passed through the state agency to:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-102(3)(a)(i): a government or local government entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-102(3)(a)(ii): a private entity, including a not-for-profit entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-102(3)(a)(iii): a person in the form of a loan or a grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-102(3)(b): The funding may come from general funds, federal funds, dedicated credits, or a combination of funding sources.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-102(4): "STEM" means science, technology, engineering, and mathematics.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201 Department of Cultural and Community Engagement -- Creation -- Powers and duties.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(1): There is created the Department of Cultural and Community Engagement.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2): (2)(a); 9-1-208; 63G-22-102; Title 63G, Chapter 22, State Training and Certification Requirements The department is responsible for:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a): planning, promoting, and supporting cultural and community engagement in the state, including programs and activities related to:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a)(i): libraries;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a)(ii): history;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a)(iii): the arts;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a)(iv): STEM engagement;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a)(v): museums;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a)(vi): cultural development;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a)(vii): cultural organizations;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a)(viii): multicultural organizations and communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a)(ix): service and volunteerism; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(a)(x): the coordination of relationships with tribal nations;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(b): overseeing and coordinating the program plans of the divisions within the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(c): (2)(a) administering and coordinating state and federal grant programs related to the programs and activities described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(d): administering any other programs over which the department is given administrative supervision by the governor;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(e): 9-1-208 submitting an annual written report to the governor and the Legislature as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(f): 63G-22-102; Title 63G, Chapter 22, State Training and Certification Requirements ensuring that any training or certification required of a public official or public employee, as those terms are defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(f)(i): under this title;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(f)(ii): by the department; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(f)(iii): by an agency or division within the department; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(2)(g): performing any other duties as provided by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(3): The department may:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(3)(a): solicit and accept contributions of money, services, and facilities from any other sources, public or private, but may not use those contributions for publicizing the exclusive interest of the donor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(3)(b): establish a nonprofit foundation called the Cultural and Community Engagement Foundation under the control and direction of the executive director to assist in the development and implementation of the programs and objectives described in this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(4): (3)(a) Money received under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(5)(a): may receive contributions of money, services, and facilities from legislative appropriations, government grants, and private sources for the development and implementation of the programs and objectives described in this title;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(5)(b): 9-1-209 shall comply with the requirements described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(5)(c): 9-1-208 shall provide information detailing all transactions and balances associated with the foundation to the department, which shall be summarized by the department and included in the department's annual report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(6): (6)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(6)(a): For a pass-through funding grant of $50,000 or less, the department shall make an annual disbursement to the pass-through funding grant recipient.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(6)(b): For a pass-through funding grant of more than $50,000, the department shall make a semiannual disbursement to the pass-through funding grant recipient, contingent upon the department receiving a semiannual progress report from the pass-through funding grant recipient.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(6)(c): (6)(b) The department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(6)(c)(i): (6)(b) provide the pass-through funding grant recipient with a progress report form for the reporting purposes described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201(6)(c)(ii): include reporting requirement instructions with the form.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201.1 Executive director of department -- Appointment -- Removal -- Compensation.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201.1(1): The department shall be directed, organized, and managed by an executive director appointed by the governor with the advice and consent of the Senate.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201.1(2): The executive director serves at the pleasure of the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201.1(3): Title 67, Chapter 22, State Officer Compensation The salary of the executive director shall be established by the governor within the salary range fixed by the Legislature in


Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201.2 Organization of department -- Jurisdiction of executive director.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The executive director:Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201.2(1): may organize the department in any fashion considered appropriate, unless otherwise expressly provided by statute; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-201.2(2): may consolidate personnel and service functions to effectuate efficiency and economy within the department.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-202 Cooperation with other agencies and organizations.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
In carrying out the provisions and purposes of this title, the department shall cooperate with, and make use of, the facilities and services of existing private or public agencies, corporations, persons, companies, or organizations to the fullest extent possible, and all state agencies, bureaus, or departments within their capabilities shall render full and complete cooperation to the department.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-203 Compliance with Administrative Procedures Act.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
The department and all of its divisions, boards, offices, bureaus, commissions, and other entities shall comply with the procedures and requirements of

Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208 Annual report -- Content -- Format.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(1): The department shall prepare and submit to the governor and the Legislature, by October 1 of each year, an annual written report of the operations, activities, programs, and services of the department, including its divisions, offices, boards, commissions, councils, and committees, for the preceding fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2): For each operation, activity, program, or service provided by the department, the annual report shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2)(a): a description of the operation, activity, program, or service;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2)(b): data selected and used by the department to measure progress, performance, and scope of the operation, activity, program, or service, including summary data;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2)(c): budget data, including the amount and source of funding, expenses, and allocation of full-time employees for the operation, activity, program, or service;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2)(d): historical data from previous years for comparison with data reported under Subsections (2)(b) and (c);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2)(e): goals, challenges, and achievements related to the operation, activity, program, or service;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2)(f): relevant federal and state statutory references and requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2)(g): contact information of officials knowledgeable and responsible for each operation, activity, program, or service; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2)(h): other information determined by the department that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2)(h)(i): may be needed, useful, or of historical significance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(2)(h)(ii): promotes accountability and transparency for each operation, activity, program, or service with the public and elected officials.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(3): The annual report shall be designed to provide clear, accurate, and accessible information to the public, the governor, and the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(4): 68-3-14 The department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(4)(a): 68-3-14 submit the annual report in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(4)(b): make the annual report, and previous annual reports, accessible to the public by placing a link to the reports on the department's website.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-208(5): 9-20-201; 9-20-301 Beginning in 2025, in addition to the annual report required by Subsection (1), the department shall provide a written report to the Education Interim Committee about the progress of the One Utah Service Fellowship Program, including the progress of the Utah Commission on Service and Volunteerism created in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-209 Cultural and Community Engagement Foundation Fund.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-209(1): As used in this section, "fund" means the Cultural and Community Engagement Foundation Fund created in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-209(2): There is created an expendable special revenue fund known as the "Cultural and Community Engagement Foundation Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-209(3): The executive director shall administer the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-209(4): Money may be deposited into the fund from a variety of sources, including transfers, grants, private foundations, individual donors, gifts, bequests, legislative appropriations, and money made available from any other source.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-209(5): 9-1-201(3)(b); (5) Money collected by the Cultural and Community Engagement Foundation described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-209(6): Any portion of the fund may be treated as an endowment fund such that the principal of that portion of the fund is held in perpetuity on behalf of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-209(7): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The state treasurer shall invest the money in the fund according to the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-209(8): The executive director may expend money from the fund for any of the purposes described in this title.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-210 Intergenerational poverty mitigation reporting.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-210(1): 35A-9-102; 35A-9-102 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-210(1)(a): 35A-9-102 "Cycle of poverty" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-210(1)(b): 35A-9-102 "Intergenerational poverty" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-210(2): 35A-9-202 On or before October 1 of each year, the department shall provide an annual report to the Department of Workforce Services for inclusion in the intergenerational poverty report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-210(3): The report shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-210(3)(a): describe policies, procedures, and programs that the department has implemented or modified to help break the cycle of poverty and end welfare dependency for children in the state affected by intergenerational poverty; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-210(3)(b): contain recommendations to the Legislature on how to address issues relating to breaking the cycle of poverty and ending welfare dependency for children in the state affected by intergenerational poverty.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211 Nonprofit Capacity Grant Program.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(1): As used in this section, "nonprofit support organization" means a nonprofit organization that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(1)(a): is organized under the Utah Revised Nonprofit Corporation Act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(1)(b): provides the following support for nonprofit organizations located in the state:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(1)(b)(i): building operational capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(1)(b)(ii): improving the delivery of essential services in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(1)(b)(iii): providing professional training;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(1)(b)(iv): providing technical support; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(1)(b)(v): encouraging collaboration with other nonprofit organizations, industry, and government agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(2)(a): There is created within the department the Nonprofit Capacity Grant Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(2)(b): The purpose of the program is to provide grants to nonprofit support organizations.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3): (1)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(a): A nonprofit support organization that submits a proposal for a grant to the department shall include details in the proposal regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(a)(i): the nonprofit support organization's name;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(a)(ii): information about the nonprofit support organization's activities and purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(a)(iii): the nonprofit support organization's budget;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(a)(iv): plans for sustaining the nonprofit support organization beyond the grant period;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(a)(v): specific proposals for how the nonprofit support organization would use the grant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(a)(vi): other information the department determines necessary to evaluate the proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(b): (1)(b) When evaluating a proposal for a grant, the department shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(b)(i): the grant amount requested;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(b)(ii): (1)(b) the extent to which the proposal advances the goals described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(b)(iii): the extent to which any additional funding sources or existing or planned partnerships may benefit the proposal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(3)(b)(iv): the viability of the proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(4): (3); Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(4)(a): eligibility criteria for a grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(4)(b): the form and process for submitting a proposal to the department for a grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(4)(c): the process and criteria for determining the priority of applications received;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(4)(d): the formula and method for determining a grant amount; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-1-211(4)(e): reporting requirements for a grant recipient.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 9 - Chapter 6 - Arts and Museums Development
************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-101 Title.
------------------------------------
This chapter is known as "Arts and Museums Development."

Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(1)(a): "Arts" means the various branches of creative human activity, including visual arts, film, performing arts, sculpture, literature, music, theater, dance, digital arts, video-game arts, and cultural vitality.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(1)(b): "Arts" includes traditional, folk, classical, ethnic, contemporary, and other art forms.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(2): 9-6-301 "Arts and museums board" means the Utah Arts and Museums Advisory Board created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(3): "Development" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(3)(a): constructing, expanding, or repairing a museum or other facility that houses arts or cultural presentations;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(3)(b): providing for public information, preservation, and access to museums, the arts, and the cultural heritage of the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(3)(c): supporting the professional development of artists, cultural administrators, and cultural leaders within the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(4): "Director" means the director of the Division of Arts and Museums.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(5): "Division" means the Division of Arts and Museums.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(6): "Museum" means an organized and permanent institution that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(6)(a): is owned or controlled by the state, a county, or a municipality, or is a nonprofit organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(6)(b): has an educational or aesthetic purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(6)(c): owns or curates a tangible collection; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(6)(d): exhibits the collection to the public on a regular schedule.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(1)(a): "Arts" means the various branches of creative human activity, including visual arts, film, performing arts, sculpture, literature, music, theater, dance, digital arts, video-game arts, and cultural vitality.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(1)(b): "Arts" includes traditional, folk, classical, ethnic, contemporary, and other art forms.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(2): 9-6-301 "Arts and museums board" means the Utah Arts and Museums Advisory Board created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(3): "Development" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(3)(a): constructing, expanding, or repairing a museum or other facility that houses arts or cultural presentations;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(3)(b): providing for public information, preservation, and access to museums, the arts, and the cultural heritage of the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(3)(c): supporting the professional development of artists, cultural administrators, and cultural leaders within the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(4): "Director" means the director of the Division of Arts and Museums.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(5): "Division" means the Division of Arts and Museums.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(6): "Museum" means an organized and permanent institution that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(6)(a): is owned or controlled by the state, a county, or a municipality, or is a nonprofit organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(6)(b): has an educational or aesthetic purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(6)(c): owns or curates a tangible collection; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-102(6)(d): exhibits the collection to the public on a regular schedule.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201 Division of Arts and Museums -- Creation -- Powers and duties.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(1): There is created within the department the Division of Arts and Museums under the administration and general supervision of the executive director or the designee of the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(a): advance the interests of arts and museums in the state in all stages of development;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(b): promote and encourage the development of arts, museums, and culture in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(c): support the efforts of state and local government and nonprofit arts, museums, and cultural organizations to encourage the development of arts, museums, and culture in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(d): provide assistance to museums in the state to improve museums' ability to:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(d)(i): care for and manage collections;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(d)(ii): develop quality educational resources such as exhibitions, collections, and publications;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(d)(iii): provide access to collections for research; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(d)(iv): provide other services as needed;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(e): assist arts and museum organizations in the state in cultural development as needed;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(f): cooperate with federal agencies and locally sponsor federal projects directed to the development of arts, museums, and culture in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(g): develop the influence of arts and museums in education and life-long learning;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(h): cooperate with the private sector, including businesses, charitable interests, educational interests, manufacturers, agriculturalists, and industrialists in arts, museums, and cultural endeavors;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(i): disseminate information related to arts, museums, and culture by utilizing broadcast media and print media;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(j): foster, promote, encourage, and facilitate the study, creation, and appreciation of the arts, museums, and culture in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(k): foster, promote, encourage, and facilitate, the study, creation, and appreciation of the works of indigenous artists in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(l): advise state and local government agencies and employees regarding arts and museums related issues, including arts and museums capital development projects;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(m): provide technical advice and information about sources of technical assistance to arts, museums, and cultural organizations in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(n): develop, coordinate, and support programs, workshops, seminars, and similar activities that provide training for staff members of arts, museums, and cultural organizations in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(o): undertake research to understand the training needs of the arts, museums, and cultural organizations community and assess how those needs can be met;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(p): administer grant programs to assist eligible arts, museums, and cultural organizations in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-201(2)(q): create strategic partnerships to advance the development of arts, museums, and cultural organizations in the state.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-202 Division director.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-202(1): The chief administrative officer of the division shall be a director appointed by the executive director in consultation with the arts and museums board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-202(2): The director shall be a person experienced in administration and knowledgeable about the arts and museums.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-202(3): 9-6-301 In addition to the division, the director is the chief administrative officer for the Utah Arts and Museums Advisory Board created in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-202 Division director.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-202(1): The chief administrative officer of the division shall be a director appointed by the executive director in consultation with the arts and museums board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-202(2): The director shall be a person experienced in administration and knowledgeable about the arts and museums.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-202(3): 9-6-301 In addition to the division, the director is the chief administrative officer for the Utah Arts and Museums Advisory Board created in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-203 Division powers relating to property.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-203(1): The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-203(1)(a): take by purchase, grant, gift, donation, devise, or bequest, any property, real or personal, for any purpose appropriate to the objectives of the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-203(1)(b): convert property received by gift, grant, donation, devise, or bequest that is not suitable for the objectives of the division, into other available property or into money.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-203(2): (1) The property received or converted under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-203(3): If by the terms of any grant, gift, donation, devise, or bequest, conditions are imposed that are impracticable under the law, the grant or donation does not fail but the unlawful or impracticable conditions shall be rejected and the intent of the grantor or donor shall be reasonably carried out as determined by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-203(4): A grant, gift, donation, devise, or bequest for the benefit of the division may not be defeated or prejudiced by any misnomer, misdescription, or informality if the intention of the grantor or donor can be shown or ascertained with reasonable certainty as determined by the division.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301 Utah Arts and Museums Advisory Board.Advisory Board.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(1): There is created within the division the Utah Arts and Museums Advisory Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(a): Except as provided in Subsections (2)(b) and (2)(g), the arts and museums board shall consist of up to 17 members appointed or reappointed by the governor to four-year terms with the advice and consent of the Senate.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(b): The governor shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of terms to ensure that the terms of arts and museums board members are staggered so that approximately half of the arts and museums board is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(c): The governor shall appoint up to seven members who are working artists or administrators, one from each of the following areas:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(c)(i): visual arts, architecture, or design;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(c)(ii): literature;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(c)(iii): music;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(c)(iv): folk, traditional, or native arts;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(c)(v): theater;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(c)(vi): dance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(c)(vii): media arts.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(d): The governor shall appoint six members who are qualified, trained, and experienced museum professionals, including three members, who each have a minimum of five years continuous paid work experience at a museum.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(e): The governor shall appoint up to two members who are knowledgeable in or appreciative of the arts or museums.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(f): The governor shall appoint up to two members who have expertise in technology, marketing, business, or finance.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(g): Before January 1, 2027, the governor may appoint up to seven additional members who are knowledgeable in or appreciative of the arts or museums:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(g)(i): for terms that shall end before June 30, 2027; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(g)(ii): in which case the arts and museums board may consist of up to 24 members until June 30, 2027.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3): The governor shall appoint members from the state with due consideration for organizational size and geographical representation.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(4): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the governor shall, within 30 days after the date on which the vacancy occurs, appoint a replacement, with the advice and consent of the Senate, for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(5): A simple majority of the voting members of the arts and museums board constitutes a quorum for the transaction of business.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(6)(a): The arts and museums board members shall elect a chair and a vice chair from among the arts and museums board's members.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(6)(b): The chair and the vice chair shall serve a term of up to two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(7): The arts and museums board shall meet at least twice each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(8): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member of the arts and museums board may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(8)(a): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(9): Except as provided in Subsection (8), a member may not receive any gifts, prizes, or awards of money from division funds during the member's term of office.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301 Utah Arts and Museums Advisory Board.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(1): There is created within the division the Utah Arts and Museums Advisory Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(a): Except as provided in Subsection (2)(b), the arts and museums board shall consist of nine members appointed or reappointed by the governor to four-year terms with the advice and consent of the Senate.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(2)(b): The governor shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of terms to ensure that the terms of arts and museums board members are staggered so that approximately half of the arts and museums board is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3): The governor shall appoint:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3)(a): five members who are working artists or administrators, one from each of the following areas:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3)(a)(i): visual arts, media arts, architecture, or design;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3)(a)(ii): literature;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3)(a)(iii): music;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3)(a)(iv): folk, traditional, or native arts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3)(a)(v): theater or dance;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3)(b): two members who are qualified, trained, and experienced museum professionals who each have a minimum of five years of continuous paid work experience at a museum;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3)(c): one member who is knowledgeable in or appreciative of the arts or museums; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(3)(d): one member who has expertise in technology, marketing, business, or finance.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(4): The governor shall appoint members described in Subsection (3) from the state at large with due consideration for geographical representation.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(5): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the governor shall, within 30 days after the date on which the vacancy occurs, appoint a replacement with the advice and consent of the Senate, for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(6): A simple majority of the voting members of the arts and museums board constitutes a quorum for the transaction of business.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(7)(a): The arts and museums board members shall elect a chair and a vice chair from among the arts and museums board's members.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(7)(b): The chair and the vice chair shall serve a term of two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(8): The arts and museums board shall meet at least twice each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(9): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member of the arts and museums board may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(9)(a): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(9)(b): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance pursuant to Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(10): Except as provided in Subsection (9), a member may not receive any gifts, prizes, or awards of money from division funds during the member's term of office.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-301(11): The division shall provide staff to the arts and museums board.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-302(1)(a): with the concurrence of the director, make rules governing the conduct of the arts and museums board's business in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-302(1)(b): receive gifts, bequests, and property.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-302(2)(a): act in an advisory capacity for the division;

Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-302 Arts and museums board powers and duties.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-302(1): The arts and museums board may:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-302(1)(a): with the concurrence of the director, make rules governing the conduct of the arts and museums board's business in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; and

Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-302(2)(a): act in an advisory capacity for the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-302(2)(b): in accordance with Subsection (3), advise the division regarding the works of art acquired and maintained under this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-302(2)(c): with the concurrence of the director, approve the allocation of arts and museums grant money and State of Utah Alice Merrill Horne Art Collection acquisition funding.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-302(3): When advising the division as described in Subsection (2)(b), the arts and museums board shall, with the concurrence of the director, appoint and consult with any combination of artists, art historians, museum professionals, gallery owners, knowledgeable art collectors, art appraisers, or judges of art.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-303 Art collection committee.
-------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-303(2)(b): The arts and museums board shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of the initial terms of arts collection committee members to ensure that the terms are staggered so that approximately half of the arts collection committee is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-6-303(3): When a vacancy occurs in the membership of the arts acquisition collection committee, the replacement shall be recommended by the remaining members of the art collection committee and then appointed by the arts and museums board with the concurrence of the director for the unexpired term.
