Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-218(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-218(4)(a): The criminal background check policy shall be distributed to qualifying prospective employees and posted in a prominent location in the public library.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-218(4)(b): A criminal background check policy adopted by a library board shall be reviewed by the library board at least every three years.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-218(5): Within appropriations made by the Legislature for this purpose, the State Library Board shall reimburse a county of the fourth, fifth, or sixth class, and a city of the fourth, fifth, or sixth class, for the costs of conducting criminal background checks under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-302 Public access.
--------------------------------------------
The public shall have access to the State Law Library.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-303 Withdrawing books.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-303(1): Books may be taken from the State Law Library by:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-303(1)(a): the members, officers, and staff of the Legislature;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-303(1)(b): the officers and staff of the executive departments and of the several boards and commissions of the state government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-303(1)(c): the justices of the Supreme Court, the judges of other state courts, and their staffs.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-303(2): No other person may withdraw any book from the State Law Library.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-304 Book register -- Time limit.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-304(1): The state law librarian shall keep a register of all books issued and returned, showing to whom issued, by whom returned, and the time issued and returned.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-304(2): No book taken from the law library may be detained more than 10 days, except by permission of the state law librarian.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-305 Injury to and failure to return books -- Action.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-305(1): If any person injures any book owned by the state law library or fails to return any book taken from the State Law Library, that person shall pay the state law librarian all loss or damage sustained because of the injury or failure to return, including costs and reasonable attorneys' fees.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-305(2): The state law librarian, in behalf of the state, shall bring action in the name of the state for the collection of all damages sustained and all losses and penalties imposed under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-307 Catalogue -- Rules.
-------------------------------------------------
The state law librarian shall catalogue all books, pamphlets, maps, charts, globes, papers, apparatus, and valuable specimens in the State Law Library and shall post in some conspicuous place a copy of the rules of the State Law Library.  The catalogue shall be made available, whether electronically or in writing, to the persons entitled to withdraw books from the State Law Library under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-308 Books to be stamped and labeled.
--------------------------------------------------------------
The state law librarian shall cause every book in the State Law Library to be labeled with a printed or stamped label containing the words "Utah State Law Library," and shall cause the same words to be written or stamped on one or more pages of each volume.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-309 Sale and exchange of books.
---------------------------------------------------------
The state law librarian may sell or exchange any surplus or duplicate sets of books in the State Law Library and use the proceeds from the sale to purchase other books for the State Law Library.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-311 Wrongful withdrawal of books -- Penalty.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
If any person not authorized by Section

Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-312 Disposition of fines and penalties.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
All fines and penalties collected pursuant to the provisions of this part shall be paid into the state treasury for the benefit of the State Law Library.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313 Law library self-help center.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(1): The Utah State Law Library shall establish a statewide self-help center to assist self-represented parties to achieve fair and efficient resolution of their cases.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(2): The self-help center shall be staffed or directed by persons admitted to the practice of law in this state.  Self-help center personnel may not represent parties or give legal advice.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(3): The self-help center shall provide to the public and all parties:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(3)(a): information about:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(3)(a)(i): the availability of mediation services, and legal advice and representation through pro bono legal services;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(3)(a)(ii): low cost legal services;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(3)(a)(iii): legal aid programs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(3)(a)(iv): lawyer referral services;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(3)(b): information about resources provided by law libraries;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(3)(c): court forms and instructions, and help completing forms;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(3)(d): answers to questions about the law, court process, and options; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-313(3)(e): educational materials and other services consistent with the purpose of this statute and the direction of the Judicial Council, including programs in other agencies and organizations.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-402 Establishment and maintenance of public library -- Library board of directors -- Expenses.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-402(1): A city's governing body may establish and maintain a public library.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-402(2): When the city governing body decides to establish and maintain a city public library under the provisions of this part, it shall appoint a library board of directors of not less than five members and not more than nine members, chosen from the citizens of the city and based upon their fitness for the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-402(3): Only one member of the city governing body may be, at any one time, a member of the library board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-402(4): Each director shall serve without compensation, but their actual and necessary expenses incurred in the performance of their official duties may be paid from library funds.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-403 Library board terms -- Officers -- Removal -- Vacancies.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-403(1): Each director of a library board shall be appointed for a three-year term, or until the successor to that director is appointed.  Initially, appointments shall be made for one-, two-, and three-year terms.  Annually thereafter, the city governing body shall, before the first day of July of each year, appoint for a three-year term directors to take the place of the retiring directors.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-403(2): Directors shall serve not more than two consecutive full terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-403(3): The directors shall annually select a chairman and other officers.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-403(4): The city governing body may remove any director for misconduct or neglect of duty.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-403(5): Vacancies in a library board of directors shall be filled for the unexpired term in the same manner as original appointments.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-404 Board powers and duties -- Library fund deposits and disbursements.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-404(1): The library board of directors may, with the approval of the city governing body:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-404(1)(a): have control of the expenditure of the library fund, of construction, lease, or sale of library buildings and land, and of the operation and care of the library; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-404(1)(b): purchase, lease, or sell land, and purchase, lease, erect, or sell buildings for the benefit of the library.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-404(2): The library board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-404(2)(a): maintain and care for the library;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-404(2)(b): establish policies for its operation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-404(2)(c): in general, carry out the spirit and intent of the provisions of this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-404(3): All tax money received for the library shall be deposited in the city treasury to the credit of the library fund, and may not be used for any purpose except that of the city library.  These funds shall be drawn upon by the authorized officers of the city upon presentation of the properly authenticated vouchers of the library board.  All money collected by the library shall be deposited to the credit of the library fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-405 Rules -- Use of library.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-405(1): The library board of directors shall make, amend, and repeal rules, not inconsistent with law, for the governing of the library.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-405(2): Each library established under this part shall be free to the use of the inhabitants of the city where located, subject to the rules adopted by the library board.  The library board may exclude from the use of the library any person who willfully violates these rules.  The library board may extend the privileges and use of the library to persons residing outside of the city upon terms and conditions it may prescribe by rule.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-406 Reports to governing body and director of the division.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The library board of directors shall:Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-406(1): provide an annual report to the city governing body on the condition and operation of the library, including a financial statement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-406(2): provide an annual report to the director of the division that contains the information required by the State Library Board.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-407 Librarian and other personnel.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-407(1): The library board of directors shall appoint a competent person as librarian to have immediate charge of the library with those duties and compensation for services that it determines. The librarian shall act as the executive officer for the library board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-407(2): The library board shall appoint, upon the recommendation of the librarian, other personnel as needed.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-408 Donations of money or property.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Any person desiring to make donations of money, personal property, or real estate for the benefit of any library shall have the right to vest the title to the money, personal property, or real estate in the library board of directors.  The donation shall be held and controlled by the library board, when accepted, according to the terms of the deed, gift, devise, or bequest of the property, and the library board shall be held and considered to be trustees of the property.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-409 Entities may cooperate, merge, or consolidate in providing library services.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Library boards of directors of city libraries, library boards of directors of county libraries, boards of education, governing boards of other educational institutions, library agencies, and local political subdivisions may cooperate, merge, or consolidate in providing library services.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-410 Consolidation with county library.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-410(1): (2) If a city library consolidates with a county library, the city library board of directors shall convey all assets and, except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-410(2): (1) If a conveyance of trust funds under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-501 Tax for establishment and maintenance of public library -- Library fund.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-501(1): A county legislative body may establish and maintain a public library.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-501(2): Part 4, City Libraries For this purpose, counties may levy annually a tax not to exceed .001 of taxable value of taxable property in the county, outside of cities which maintain their own city libraries as authorized by
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-501(3): The taxes shall be levied and collected in the same manner as other general taxes of the county and shall constitute a fund to be known as the county library fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-502 Library board of directors -- Expenses.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-502(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-502(1)(a): When the county legislative body decides to establish and maintain a county public library under the provisions of this part, the county executive shall, with the advice and consent of the county legislative body, appoint a library board of not less than five and not more than nine directors chosen from the citizens of the county and based upon their fitness for the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-502(1)(b): When increasing membership on an existing library board, the county legislative body:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-502(1)(b)(i): may not add more than two positions in any year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-502(1)(b)(ii): when adding members, shall ensure that the terms of library board members are staggered so that approximately 1/4 of the board is selected each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-502(2): Only one member of the county legislative body may be, at any one time, a member of the library board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-502(3): Each director shall serve without compensation, but the actual and necessary expenses incurred in the performance of the director's official duties may be paid from library funds.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-503 Library board terms -- Officers -- Removal -- Vacancies.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-503(1): Each director of a library board shall be appointed for a four-year term, or until the director's successor is appointed.   Initially, appointments shall be made for one-, two-, three-, and four-year terms, and one member of the county legislative body for the term of his elected office.   Annually thereafter, the county executive body shall, before the first day of July of each year, appoint, with the advice and consent of the county legislative body, for a four-year term, one director to take the place of the retiring director.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-503(2): Directors shall serve not more than two consecutive full terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-503(3): The directors shall annually select a chairman and other officers.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-503(4): The county executive body may remove any director for misconduct or neglect of duty.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-503(5): Vacancies in a library board of directors shall be filled for the unexpired terms in the same manner as original appointments.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504 Library board duties -- Library fund deposits.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504(1): The library board of directors shall, with the approval of the county executive and in accordance with county ordinances, policies, and procedures:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504(1)(a): be responsible for:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504(1)(a)(i): the expenditure of the library fund;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504(1)(a)(ii): the construction, lease, or sale of library buildings and land; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504(1)(a)(iii): the operation and care of the library; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504(1)(b): purchase, lease, or sell land, and purchase, lease, construct, or sell buildings, for the benefit of the library.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504(2): The library board has those powers and duties as prescribed by county ordinance, including establishing policies for collections and information resources that are consistent with state and federal law.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504(3)(a): All tax money received for the library shall be deposited in the county treasury to the credit of the library fund, and may not be used for any purpose except that of the county library.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-504(3)(b): All money collected by the library shall be deposited to the credit of the library fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-505 Rules -- Use of library.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-505(1): Each library board shall make library rules in a manner consistent with county ordinances, policies, and procedures for the governing of the library.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-505(2): Each library established under this part shall be free to the use of the inhabitants of the area taxed for the support of the library, subject to the rules made as prescribed by county ordinance.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-506 Annual reports.
---------------------------------------------
The library board of directors shall:Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-506(1): provide an annual report to the county executive and county legislative body on the condition and operation of the library, including a financial statement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-506(2): provide an annual report to the director of the division that contains the information required by the State Library Board.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-507 Librarian and other personnel.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-507(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-507(1)(a): The library board of directors shall recommend to the county executive for appointment a competent person to serve as librarian.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-507(1)(b): The county executive shall, within 30 days of the recommendation, either make the appointment or request that the library board submit another recommendation.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-507(1)(c): The librarian shall be an employee of the county subject to the personnel policies, procedures, and compensation plans approved by the county executive and county legislative body.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-507(1)(d): The librarian shall act as the executive officer for the library board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-507(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-507(2)(a): All library personnel are employees of the county.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-507(2)(b): The librarian or the librarian's designee shall hire library personnel in accordance with the county merit system, personnel policies and procedures, and compensation plans approved by the county executive and county legislative body.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-507(3): As used in this section "librarian" means the county library director.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-508 Donations of money or property.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-508(1): A person desiring to make a donation of money, personal property, or real estate for the benefit of a library has the right to vest the title to the money, personal property, or real estate in the county, designated for the benefit and purposes of the library.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-508(2): The county shall hold donated personal property and real estate as prescribed by county ordinance according to the terms of the deed, gift, devise, or bequest of the property, and the county shall be the trustee of the property.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-509 Entities may cooperate, merge, or consolidate in providing library services.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Library boards of directors of city libraries, library boards of directors of county libraries, boards of education, governing boards of other educational institutions, library agencies, and local political subdivisions may cooperate in providing library services or merge or consolidate under an interlocal agreement approved and implemented in accordance with

Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-510 Estimate of money.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-510(1): The library board of directors shall furnish to the county executive and county legislative body, in writing, and prior to the time required by law to levy county taxes, an estimate of the amount of money necessary to establish, equip, and maintain the library, and to provide library services during the next ensuing fiscal year and shall certify the amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-510(2): The county legislative body may, at the time and in the manner of levying other taxes, impose the levy, but the levy may not exceed in any one year .001 per dollar of taxable value of taxable property in the county.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-511 Library bonds -- Issuance of previously voted bonds.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-511(1): When an election has been held in any county to authorize bonds of the county for the purpose of acquiring, improving, and extending a public library for the county, including the acquisition of equipment, furnishings, and books, and it was specified in the proposition that the bonds are to be payable from ad valorem taxes to be levied on all taxable property in the county, and when the election has carried, but none of the bonds authorized have been issued, the bonds authorized to be issued at election may be issued and shall be payable from taxes to be levied without limitation as to rate or amount on all taxable property in the county, despite any provision of law to the contrary in effect at the time of the election.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-7-511(2): All county library bonds that have been authorized but not yet issued, all county library bond elections previously held and carried, and all proceedings in connection with them that were adopted for the authorization of the bonds are hereby validated, ratified, approved, and confirmed, and the bonds, when issued in accordance with the election and proceedings, shall be binding, legal, valid, and enforceable obligations of the county issuing them in accordance with their terms.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 9 - Chapter 8 - History Development
***************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-102 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-102(1): "Board" means the Board of State History.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-102(2): "Director" means the director of the Utah Historical Society.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-102(3): "Documentary materials" means written or documentary information contained in published materials, manuscript collections, archival materials, photographs, sound recordings, motion pictures, and other written, visual, and aural materials, except government records.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-102(4): "Historical artifacts" means objects produced or shaped by human efforts, a natural object deliberately selected and used by a human, an object of aesthetic interest, and any human-made objects produced, used, or valued by the historic peoples of Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-102(5): 9-8-209 "Museum of Utah" means the Museum of Utah created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-102(6): 9-8-201 "Society" means the Utah Historical Society created in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-201 Utah Historical Society -- Creation -- Purpose.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-201(1): There is created within the department the Utah Historical Society under the administration and general supervision of the executive director or the designee of the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-201(2): The division, with the advisement of the board, shall be the authority of the state for state history and shall perform those duties set forth in statute.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-202 Appointment of director.
------------------------------------------------------
The executive director, in consultation with the board, shall appoint a director of the society:Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-202(1): to serve as the chief administrative officer of the society; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-202(2): who is experienced in administration and is qualified by education or training in the field of state history.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203 Society duties.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1): 63G-1-401 The society shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(a): stimulate research, study, and activity in the field of Utah history and related history;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(b): maintain a specialized history library;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(c): collect, preserve, and administer historical records relating to the history of Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(d): administer, collect, preserve, document, interpret, develop, and exhibit historical artifacts, documentary materials, and other objects relating to the history of Utah for educational and cultural purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(e): edit and publish historical records;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(f): cooperate with local, state, and federal agencies and schools and museums to provide coordinated and organized activities for the collection, documentation, preservation, interpretation, and exhibition of historical artifacts related to the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(g): 63G-1-401 promote, coordinate, and administer:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(g)(i): 63G-1-401 Utah History Day at the Capitol designated under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(g)(ii): the Utah History Day program affiliated with National History Day, which includes a series of regional, state, and national activities and competitions for students from grades 4 through 12;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(h): subject to legislative appropriations, provide grants and technical assistance as necessary and appropriate;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(i): administer educational programs in partnership with public and private entities in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(1)(j): comply with the procedures and requirements of Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act, in adjudicative proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(2): 63A-2-101.5; 63A-2-401
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(2)(a): The society may acquire or produce reproductions of historical artifacts and documentary materials for educational and cultural use.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(2)(b): The society may only deaccession an item described in Subsection (2)(a) in accordance with rules made by the division in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(2)(c): 63A-2-101.5; 63A-2-401 An item that is to be deaccessioned in accordance with society rule is not state surplus property as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(3): To promote an appreciation of Utah history and to increase heritage tourism in the state, the society shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(3)(a): create and maintain an inventory of all historic markers and monuments that are accessible to the public throughout the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(3)(b): enter into cooperative agreements with other groups and organizations to collect and maintain the information needed for the inventory described in Subsection (3)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(3)(c): encourage the use of volunteers to help collect the information and to maintain the inventory described in Subsection (3)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(3)(d): publicize the information in the inventory described in Subsection (3)(a) in a variety of forms and media, especially to encourage Utah citizens and tourists to visit the markers and monuments;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(3)(e): work with public and private landowners, heritage organizations, and volunteer groups to help maintain, repair, and landscape around the markers and monuments; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(3)(f): make the inventory described in Subsection (3)(a) available upon request to all other public and private history and heritage organizations, tourism organizations and businesses, and others.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-203(4): This chapter may not be construed to authorize the society to acquire by purchase any historical artifacts, documentary materials, or specimens that are restricted from sale by federal law or the laws of any state, territory, or foreign nation.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204 Board of State History.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(1): There is created within the department the Board of State History.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(2): The board shall consist of 11 members appointed or reappointed by the governor with the advice and consent of the Senate, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 24, Part 2, Vacancies, who are persons with an interest in the subject matter of the society's responsibilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(3)(a): Except as required by Subsection (3)(b), the members shall be appointed for terms of four years and shall serve until their successors are appointed and qualified.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(3)(b): Notwithstanding the requirements of Subsection (3)(a), the governor shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of terms to ensure that the terms of board members are staggered so that approximately half of the board is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(4): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the governor shall, with the advice and consent of the Senate in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 24, Part 2, Vacancies, appoint a replacement for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(5): A simple majority of the board constitutes a quorum for conducting board business.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(6): The governor shall select a chair and vice chair from the board members.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(7): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(7)(a): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(7)(b): 63A-3-107 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(7)(c): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance pursuant to Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-204(8): A member shall comply with the conflict of interest provisions described in Title 63G, Chapter 24, Part 3, Conflicts of Interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-205 Board duties and powers.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-205(1): The board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-205(1)(a): make policies to direct the director in carrying out the director's duties;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-205(1)(b): approve the society's rules; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-205(1)(c): make recommendations to the society for the development of programs consistent with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-205(2): The board may establish subcommittees to assist the board, the office, and the society in carrying out the responsibilities under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-206 Historical magazine, books, documents, and microfilms -- Proceeds.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-206(1): The society shall, under the direction of the board:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-206(1)(a): compile and publish an historical magazine to be furnished to supporting members of the society in accordance with membership subscriptions or to be sold independently of membership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-206(1)(b): publish and sell other books, documents, and microfilms at reasonable prices to be approved by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-206(2): Proceeds from sales under this section shall be deposited into the General Fund as a dedicated credit.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-207 Donations -- Accounting.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-207(1): The society may:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-207(1)(a): solicit memberships from persons interested in the work of the society and charge dues for memberships commensurate with the advantages of membership and the needs of the society; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-207(1)(b): receive gifts, donations, bequests, devises, and endowments of money or property, which shall then become the property of the state of Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-207(2): (1)(b); (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-207(2)(a): (1)(b) If the donor directs that money or property donated under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-207(2)(b): (2)(a) Except as provided in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-209 Museum of Utah -- Creation -- Duties.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-209(1): There is created within the society the Museum of Utah under the administration and supervision of the director or the designee of the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-209(2): The Museum of Utah shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-209(2)(a): function as an educational outlet for the society to educate the public on Utah history and culture;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-209(2)(b): support the efforts of museums, historical organizations, and other cultural organizations in the state to promote and preserve Utah history and culture;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-209(2)(c): serve as a repository of historical artifacts acquired by the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-209(2)(d): stimulate research, study, and activity in the field of Utah history, museum studies, and related fields of study;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-209(2)(e): exhibit collections to the public on a regular schedule;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-209(2)(f): facilitate strategic partnerships to advance the development of museums, historical organizations, and other cultural organizations in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-209(2)(g): establish and coordinate best practices among museum professionals and volunteers in the state.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-701 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-701(1): "Endowment fund" means any history endowment fund created under this part by a qualifying organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-701(2): "Qualifying organization" means any Utah nonprofit history organization or local government that qualifies under this chapter to create an endowment fund, receive state money into the endowment fund, match state money deposited into the endowment fund, and expend interest earned on the endowment fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703 History organization endowment funds.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(1): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(1)(a): A qualifying organization may create an endowment fund into which there may be deposited money from funds made available for that purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(1)(b): The principal of each endowment fund may not be expended by the qualifying organization and shall be held in perpetuity solely by the qualifying organization or by the Division of Finance on behalf of the qualifying organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(1)(c): Only interest income earned on the amount in each endowment fund may be expended by the qualifying organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(1)(d): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The principal of each endowment fund shall be invested in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(2)(a): An endowment fund shall be administered in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles by professional endowment management personnel.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(2)(b): If no professional endowment management personnel is available to the qualifying organization, the qualifying organization shall place the endowment fund in a state fiduciary fund administered by the Division of Finance.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(3): If an endowment fund is administered by the Division of Finance:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(3)(a): the Division of Finance shall allocate interest income to the qualifying organization annually; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-703(3)(b): the costs for the administration shall be deducted from the interest income before allocations of interest income may be made to the qualifying organization by the Division of Finance.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-704(2): determine the eligibility of each qualifying organization to receive money from funds made available for that purpose into the endowment fund of the qualifying organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-704(3): determine the matching amount each qualifying organization must raise in order to qualify to receive money from funds made available for that purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-704(4): establish a date by which each qualifying organization must provide the qualifying organization's matching funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-704(5): (4) verify that matching funds have been provided by each qualifying organization by the date determined in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705 Eligibility requirements of qualifying history organizations -- Allocation limitations -- Matching requirements.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(1): 9-8-703; (1) A qualifying organization may apply to receive money from funds made available for that purpose to be deposited into an endowment fund created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(1)(a): (1) received a grant from the society during one of the three years immediately before making application for money under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(1)(b): not received a grant from the society within the past three years, the qualifying organization may receive a grant upon approval by the society according to policy of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(2)(a): The maximum amount that may be allocated to each qualifying organization from funds made available for that purpose shall be determined by the society in a format to be developed in consultation with the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(2)(b): The minimum amount that may be allocated to each qualifying organization from funds made available for that purpose is $2,500.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(3)(a): After the society determines that a qualifying organization is eligible to receive money from funds made available for that purpose and before any money is allocated to the qualifying organization from available funds, the qualifying organization shall match the amount qualified for by money raised and designated exclusively for that purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(3)(b): State money and in-kind contributions may not be used to match money from funds made available for that purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(4): Endowment match money shall be based on a sliding scale as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(4)(a): amounts requested up to $20,000 shall be matched one-to-one;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(4)(b): any additional amount requested that makes the aggregate amount requested exceed $20,000 but not exceed $50,000 shall be matched two-to-one; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(4)(c): any additional amount requested that makes the aggregate amount requested exceed $50,000 shall be matched three-to-one.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(5): (5)(a); (5)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(5)(a): Qualifying organizations shall raise the matching amount by a date determined by the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(5)(b): (5)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(5)(b)(i): (5)(a) Money from funds made available for that purpose shall be released to the qualifying organization upon verification by the society that the matching money has been received on or before the date determined under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(5)(b)(ii): Verification of matching funds shall be made by a certified public accountant.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(5)(c): Money from funds made available for that purpose shall be released to qualifying organizations with professional endowment management in increments of at least $2,500 as audited confirmation of matching funds is received by the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-705(5)(d): (5)(a) Money from funds made available for that purpose shall be granted to each qualifying organization on the basis of the matching funds the qualifying organization has raised by the date determined under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-708 Federal match.
--------------------------------------------
Funds allocated by the society under this part to enable qualifying organizations to create their own endowment funds may be construed as a state match for any history funding from the federal government that may be provided.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-801 Short title.
------------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Preserve Our Heritage Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-802 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-802(1): "Agency" means any administrative unit of Utah's state government or local government.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-802(2): "Collecting institutions" means historical societies, museums, archives, and libraries that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-802(2)(a): are operated by nonprofit corporations in Utah or by any Utah agency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-802(2)(b): preserve our heritage and benefit society by acquiring and preserving reposited materials.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-802(3): "Reposited materials" means materials of historical, artistic, literary, or scientific value that are deposited in a collecting institution.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-803 Ownership of reposited materials -- Rebuttable presumption.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-803(1): There is established a rebuttable presumption that any reposited materials held by a collecting institution are the property of that collecting institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-803(2): Any person seeking to claim reposited materials from a collecting institution shall comply with the requirements of this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-804 Statute of limitations for claiming reposited materials from a collecting institution.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-804(1): Any reposited materials in a collecting institution that are not accompanied by a transfer of title to those materials are considered a gift to the collecting institution when more than 25 years have passed from the date of the last written contact between the depositor or his successors and the collecting institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-804(2): No depositor or any of his successors may bring an action against the collecting institution to recover the reposited materials from the collecting institution after 25 years have passed from the date of the last written contact between the depositor or his successors and the collecting institution.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-805 Collecting institutions -- Perfecting title -- Notice.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-805(1): (2); (1)(a); (2); (1)(b); 63G-30-102; 45-1-101
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-805(1)(a): (2) A collecting institution wishing to perfect title in any reposited materials held by it shall send, by registered mail, a notice containing the information required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-805(1)(b): (1)(a); (2) In addition to the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-805(1)(b)(i): the owner or the address of the owner of the reposited materials is unknown;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-805(1)(b)(ii): the mailed notice is returned to the collecting institution without a forwarding address; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-805(1)(b)(iii): the owner does not claim the reposited materials within 90 days after the day on which the notice was mailed.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-805(1)(c): (1)(b); 63G-30-102; 45-1-101 If required to publish a notice under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-805(1)(c)(i): 63G-30-102 for the county where the collecting institution is located, as a class A notice under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-805(2)(d): (1)(b) a statement that if the reposited materials are not claimed within 90 days from the day on which the notice is published in accordance with Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-806 Claiming reposited materials held by a collecting institution.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-806(1): Any person claiming title to reposited materials held by a collecting institution shall demonstrate that he owns all right, title, and interest in the reposited materials to the reasonable satisfaction of the collecting institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-806(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-806(2)(a): Any person claiming to represent a person claiming title to reposited materials held by a collecting institution shall demonstrate, to the reasonable satisfaction of the collecting institution, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-806(2)(a)(i): he represents every person who owns any right, title, or interest in the reposited materials; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-806(2)(a)(ii): the persons he represents own all right, title, and interest in the reposited materials.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8-806(2)(b): Any person claiming he represents persons holding all right, title, and interest in the reposited materials may demonstrate that representation by providing the collecting institution with a notarized authorization from every person having any right, title, or interest in the reposited materials.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 9 - Chapter 8a - State Historic Preservation Office
*******************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-101 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-101(1): 9-8-204 "Board" means the Board of State History created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-101(2): 9-8a-204 "Committee" means the National Register Review Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-101(3): 9-8a-201 "Office" means the State Historic Preservation Office created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-101(4): 9-8a-202 "Officer" means the state historic preservation officer, appointed in accordance with Section


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-201 State Historic Preservation Office -- Creation -- Purpose.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-201(1): There is created within the department the State Historic Preservation Office under the administration and supervision of the executive director or the designee of the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-201(2): The office shall be under the policy direction of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-201(3): The office shall be the authority in the state for state history preservation and shall perform those duties set forth in statute.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-202 Appointment of state historic preservation officer.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-202(1): In accordance with 36 C.F.R. Sec. 61.4, the governor shall appoint the state historic preservation officer.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-202(2): The officer shall administer:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-202(2)(a): the office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-202(2)(b): the state historic preservation program.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203 Office duties.
---------------------------------------------
The office shall:Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(1): secure, for the present and future benefit of the state, the protection of archaeological resources and sites which are on state lands;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(2): foster increased cooperation and exchange of information between state authorities, the professional archaeological community, and private individuals;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(3): in cooperation with federal and state agencies, local governments, private organizations, and private individuals, direct and conduct a comprehensive statewide survey of historic properties;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(4): maintain an inventory of the properties described in Subsection (3);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(5): identify and nominate eligible property to the National Register of Historic Places;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(6): administer applications for listing historic property on the National Register of Historic Places;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(7): prepare and implement a comprehensive statewide historic preservation plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(8): administer the state program of federal assistance for historic preservation within the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(9): advise and assist, as appropriate, state agencies, federal agencies, and local governments in carrying out their historic preservation responsibilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(10): cooperate with federal agencies, state agencies, local agencies, private organizations, and individuals to ensure that historic property is taken into consideration at all levels of planning and development;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(11): provide, with respect to historic preservation:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(11)(a): public information;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(11)(b): education;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(11)(c): training; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(11)(d): technical assistance;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(12): cooperate with local governments in the development of local historic preservation programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(13): consult with appropriate federal agencies with respect to:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(13)(a): federal undertakings that may affect historic properties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(13)(b): advising and assisting in the evaluation of proposals for rehabilitation projects that may qualify for federal assistance;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(14): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(14)(a): create and maintain an inventory of all active and inactive cemeteries throughout the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(14)(b): enter into cooperative agreements with local governments and other groups and organizations to collect and maintain the information needed for the inventory described in Subsection (14)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(14)(c): encourage the use of volunteers to help collect the information and to maintain the inventory described in Subsection (14)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(14)(d): encourage cemetery owners, or in the case of inactive or small historic cemeteries, volunteers, to create and maintain geographic information systems to record burial sites;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(14)(e): publicize the information in the inventory described in Subsection (14)(a) in a variety of forms and media, especially to encourage Utah citizens to participate in the care and upkeep of historic cemeteries;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(14)(f): work with public and private cemeteries, heritage organizations, genealogical groups, and volunteer groups to help maintain, repair, and landscape cemeteries, grave sites, and tombstones; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(14)(g): make the inventory described in Subsection (14)(a) available to any person upon request;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(15): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(15)(a): create and maintain a public electronic record of each cemetery location and each burial location;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(15)(b): help maintain, repair, and landscape cemeteries, grave sites, and tombstones by providing matching grants to:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(15)(b)(i): municipal cemeteries;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(15)(b)(ii): cemetery maintenance districts;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(15)(b)(iii): endowment care cemeteries;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(15)(b)(iv): private nonprofit cemeteries;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(15)(b)(v): genealogical associations; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(15)(b)(vi): other nonprofit groups with an interest in cemeteries; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(15)(c): make rules, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, governing the process for awarding grants under Subsection (15)(b), including rules that ensure recipients use grant money for projects that are cost effective and completed in accordance with applicable professional standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(16): perform other duties as designated under 54 U.S.C. Sec. 302303; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-203(17): perform other duties as designated by the department and by statute.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-204 National Register Review Committee.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-204(1): There is created the National Register Review Committee.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-204(2)(b): prehistoric and historic archaeology;

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-204(2)(g): museology, curation, or conservation;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-204(2)(h): landscape architecture; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-204(2)(i): planning.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-204(3): (2) To qualify as a member with professional experience in a discipline described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-204(14)(d): recommend the removal of properties from the National Register of Historic Places;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-204(14)(e): assist the officer and the office in statewide efforts to encourage public and private persons to identify, nominate, protect, enhance, and maintain the state's historic resources; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-204(14)(f): review the State Historic Preservation Plan prior to submission to the United States  Department of the Interior.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205 Cultural Site Stewardship Program -- Definitions -- Creation -- Objectives -- Administration -- Activities.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(1): 9-8a-302; 79-3-102 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(1)(a): 9-8a-302; 79-3-102
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(1)(a)(i): "Cultural site" means a significant archaeological or paleontological site in the state as determined by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(1)(a)(ii): 9-8a-302; 79-3-102 "Cultural site" may include a:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(1)(a)(ii)(A): 9-8a-302 site as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(1)(a)(ii)(B): 79-3-102 site as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(1)(b): "Stewardship program" means the Cultural Site Stewardship Program created in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(1)(c): "Vandalism" means to damage, destroy, or commit any other act that defaces or harms a cultural site without the consent of the owner or appropriate governmental agency, including inscribing, marking, etching, scratching, drawing, painting on, or affixing to the cultural resource a mark, figure, or design.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(2): There is created within the office the Cultural Site Stewardship Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(3): 9-8a-304(2)(b); 79-3-202(1)(m) The office shall seek to accomplish the following objectives through administration of the stewardship program:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(3)(a): protect cultural sites located in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(3)(b): increase public awareness of the significance and value of cultural sites and the damage done to cultural sites by vandalism;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(3)(c): discourage vandalism and the unlawful sale and trade of archaeological artifacts and paleontological artifacts;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(3)(d): support and encourage improved standards for investigating and researching cultural sites in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(3)(e): promote cooperation among governmental agencies, private landowners, Native American tribes, industry groups, and interested persons to protect cultural sites; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(3)(f): 9-8a-304(2)(b); 79-3-202(1)(m) increase the inventory of cultural sites maintained in accordance with Subsections

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(4)(b): provide administrative services to the stewardship program.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-205(5): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The office shall select, train, and certify volunteers to participate in the stewardship program, based on rules made by the office in accordance with

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-206(2)(b): by direct payment to the landowner or a third party for work related to identifying and protecting archaeological resources on the landowner's property, if the private landowner or third party contributes an amount of money or in-kind work equal to or greater than the amount of money received from the grant program.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-301 Purpose.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-301(1): The Legislature declares that the general public and the beneficiaries of the school and institutional land grants have an interest in the preservation and protection of the state's archaeological and anthropological resources and a right to the knowledge derived and gained from scientific study of those resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-301(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-301(2)(a): The Legislature finds that policies and procedures for the survey and excavation of archaeological resources from school and institutional trust lands are consistent with the school and institutional land grants, if these policies and procedures insure that primary consideration is given, on a site or project specific basis, to the purpose of support for the beneficiaries of the school and institutional land grants.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-301(2)(b): The Legislature finds that the preservation, placement in a repository, curation, and exhibition of specimens found on school or institutional trust lands for scientific and educational purposes is consistent with the school and institutional land grants.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-301(2)(c): The Legislature finds that the preservation and development of sites found on school or institutional trust lands for scientific or educational purposes, or the disposition of sites found on school or institutional trust lands, after consultation between the office and the School and Institutional Trust Lands Administration to determine the appropriate level of data recovery or implementation of other appropriate preservation measures, for preservation, development, or economic purposes, is consistent with the school and institutional land grants.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-301(2)(d): The Legislature declares that specimens found on lands owned or controlled by the state or its subdivisions may not be sold.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-301(3): The Legislature declares that the historical preservation purposes of this chapter must be kept in balance with the other uses of land and natural resources which benefit the health and welfare of the state's citizens.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-301(4): Part 4, Historic Sites It is the purpose of this part and


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part andUtah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(1): "Agency" means a department, division, office, bureau, board, commission, or other administrative unit of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(2): "Ancient human remains" means all or part of the following that are historic or prehistoric:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(2)(a): a physical individual; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(2)(b): any object on or attached to the physical individual that is placed on or attached to the physical individual as part of the death rite or ceremony of a culture.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(3): 9-8a-304 "Antiquities Section" means the Antiquities Section of the office created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(4): "Archaeological resources" means all material remains and their associations, recoverable or discoverable through excavation or survey, that provide information pertaining to the historic or prehistoric peoples of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(5): "Collection" means a specimen and the associated records documenting the specimen and the specimen's recovery.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(6): "Curation" means management and care of collections according to standard professional museum practice, which may include inventorying, accessioning, labeling, cataloging, identifying, evaluating, documenting, storing, maintaining, periodically inspecting, cleaning, stabilizing, conserving, exhibiting, exchanging, or otherwise disposing of original collections or reproductions, and providing access to and facilities for studying collections.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(7): 53B-17-603 "Curation facility" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(8): "Excavate" means the recovery of archaeological resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(9): "Historic property" means any prehistoric or historic district, site, building, structure, or specimen included in, or eligible for inclusion in, the National Register of Historic Places or the State Register.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(10): "Indian tribe" means a tribe, band, nation, or other organized group or community of Indians that is recognized as eligible for the special programs and services provided by the United States to Indians because of their status as Indians.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(11): "Museum" means the Utah Museum of Natural History.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(12): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(12)(a): "Nonfederal land" means land in the state that is not owned, controlled, or held in trust by the federal government.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(12)(b): "Nonfederal land" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(12)(b)(i): land owned or controlled by:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(12)(b)(i)(A): the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(12)(b)(i)(B): a county, city, or town;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(12)(b)(i)(C): an Indian tribe, if the land is not held in trust by the United States for the Indian tribe or the Indian tribe's members; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(12)(b)(i)(D): a person other than the federal government; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(12)(b)(ii): school and institutional trust lands.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(13): "Principal investigator" means the individual with overall administrative responsibility for the survey or excavation project authorized by the permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(14): 53B-17-603 "Repository" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(15): 53C-1-103 "School and institutional trust lands" are those properties defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(16): "Site" means any petroglyphs, pictographs, structural remains, or geographic location that is the source of archaeological resources or specimens.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(17): "Specimen" means all man-made artifacts and remains of an archaeological or anthropological nature found on or below the surface of the earth, excluding structural remains.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(18): 53B-3-102
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(18)(a): 53B-3-102 "State land" means land owned by the state including the state's:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(18)(a)(i): legislative and judicial branches;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(18)(a)(ii): departments, divisions, agencies, boards, commissions, councils, and committees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(18)(a)(iii): 53B-3-102 institutions of higher education as defined under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(18)(b): "State land" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(18)(b)(i): land owned by a political subdivision of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(18)(b)(ii): land owned by a school district;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(18)(b)(iii): private land; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(18)(b)(iv): school and institutional trust lands.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(19): "Survey" means a surface investigation for archaeological resources that may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(19)(a): insubstantial surface collection of archaeological resources; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-302(19)(b): limited subsurface testing that disturbs no more of a site than is necessary to determine the nature and extent of the archaeological resources or whether the site is a historic property.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-306 Archaeological or anthropological landmarks.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-306(1): Sites of significance may be recommended to and approved by the board as state archaeological or anthropological landmarks.  No privately owned site or site on school or institutional trust lands may be so designated without the written consent of the owner.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-306(2): A person may not excavate upon a privately owned designated landmark without a permit from the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-306(3): Before any alteration is commenced on a designated landmark, three months' notice of intent to alter the site shall be provided to the office.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-307 Report of discovery on state or private lands.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-307(1): Any person who discovers any archaeological resources on lands owned or controlled by the state or its subdivisions shall promptly report the discovery to the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-307(2): Any person who discovers any archaeological resources on privately owned lands shall promptly report the discovery to the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-307(3): Part 4, Historic Sites Field investigations shall be discouraged except in accordance with this part and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-307(4): Nothing in this section may be construed to authorize any person to survey or excavate for archaeological resources.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-308 Forgery or false labeling of specimens unlawful.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
It is unlawful to reproduce, rework, or forge any specimen or make any object, whether copied or not, or falsely label, describe, identify, or offer for sale or exchange any object, with intent to represent it as an original and genuine specimen.  No person may offer for sale or other exchange any object with knowledge that it was collected or excavated in violation of this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-401 Purpose.
---------------------------------------
The Legislature determines and declares that the public has a vital interest in all antiquities, historic and prehistoric ruins, and historic sites, buildings, and objects which, when neglected, desecrated, destroyed or diminished in aesthetic value, result in an irreplaceable loss to the people of this state.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402 Definitions -- Office duties.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(1): 9-8a-302 In addition to the definitions described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(1)(a): "Effect" means an alteration to one or more characteristics of a historic property that qualify the historic property for inclusion in, or that make the historic property eligible for inclusion in, the National Register of Historic Places.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(1)(b): "Historic property" means any historic or prehistoric district, site, building, structure, or object that is at least 50 years old and that is included in, or that is eligible for inclusion in, the National Register of Historic Places.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(1)(c): "State register" means a register of cultural sites and localities, historic and prehistoric sites, and districts, buildings, and objects significant in Utah history.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(1)(d): "Undertaking" means a project, activity, or program funded in whole or in part under the direct or indirect jurisdiction of a state agency, including a project, activity, or program:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(1)(d)(i): carried out by or on behalf of a state agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(1)(d)(ii): carried out with financial assistance from the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(1)(d)(iii): that requires a state permit, license, or approval.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(2): The office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(2)(a): constitute the historic preservation agency for this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(2)(b): establish a state register for the orderly identification and recognition of the state's cultural resources; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-402(2)(c): provide for participation in the National Historic Preservation Program.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-403 Placement on State or National Register.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
The board shall notify owners of sites, buildings, structures, or objects before placing those sites, buildings, structures, or objects on the State Register or nominating them to the National Register.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-405 Federal funds -- Agreements on standards and procedures.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
By following the procedures and requirements of

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-502 Legislative finding.
---------------------------------------------------
The Legislature finds and declares that preservation and restoration of historically significant real property and structures as identified by the State Register of Historic Sites are in the public interest of the people of the state of Utah and should be promoted by the laws of this state.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-503 Preservation easement.
-----------------------------------------------------
Any owner of a fee simple interest in real property may convey, and any other party entitled to own real property interests may accept, a preservation easement pertaining to the real property if the real property possesses historical value that will be enhanced or preserved by the terms of the easement regarding restoration or preservation of the real property.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-504 Preservation easement -- Subject to other laws.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Except as provided in this part, preservation easements are subject to the other laws of this state governing easements, generally.  Any preservation easement may, with respect to the burdened land, entitle its owner to take certain action, to require certain action to be taken by the owner of the burdened land, or require that certain action not be taken by the owner of the burdened land, and under any such circumstances may be either appurtenant or in gross.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-505 Rule Against Perpetuities and Rule Restricting Unreasonable Restraints on Alienation not applicable.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The rule of property known as the Rule Against Perpetuities and the rule of property known as the Rule Restricting Unreasonable Restraints on Alienation may not be applied to defeat any of the provisions of this part or of any deed, lease, conveyance, covenant, easement, or other interest created or document executed in accordance with the provisions of this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-8a-506 Charitable contribution for tax purposes.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any conveyance of a preservation easement may be deemed a charitable contribution for tax purposes in accordance with the laws, rules, and regulations pertaining to charitable contributions of interests in real property.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 9 - Chapter 9 - Utah Division of Indian Affairs Act
*******************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-101 Title -- Definitions.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-101(1): This chapter is known as the "Utah Division of Indian Affairs Act."
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-101(2): 9-9-102
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-101(2)(a): 9-9-102 As used in this chapter, "division" means the Utah Division of Indian Affairs created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-101(2)(b): As used in this part, "Indian tribe" or "tribe" means a tribe, band, nation, or other organized group or community of Indians that is recognized as eligible for the special programs and services provided by the United States to Indians because of their status as Indians.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-102 Division of Indian Affairs created -- Supervision by department.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-102(1): There is created within the department a Utah Division of Indian Affairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-102(2): The division shall be under the administration and general supervision of the department.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-103 Purpose.
--------------------------------------
The division shall:Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-103(1): develop programs that will allow Indian citizens residing on or off reservations an opportunity to share in the progress of Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-103(2): promote an atmosphere in which Indian citizens are provided alternatives so that individual citizens may choose for themselves the kinds of lives they will live, both socially and economically;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-103(3): promote programs to help the tribes and Indian communities find and implement solutions to their community problems; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-103(4): promote government-to-government relations between the state and tribal governments.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104 Duties and powers.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(1): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(1)(a): have all of the functions, powers, duties, rights, and responsibilities granted to it by this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(1)(b): staff those committees or boards as specified in this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(1)(c): in accordance with policies set by state government, coordinate relations between:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(1)(c)(i): the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(1)(c)(ii): tribal governments;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(1)(c)(iii): other Indian groups; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(1)(c)(iv): federal agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (2)(d) The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(2)(a): contract with public and private entities to provide services or facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-104(2)(b): acquire and hold funds or other property for the administration of the programs outlined in this chapter;
