Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-201 Assumption by state of criminal and civil jurisdiction over Indians and Indian territory.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The state of Utah hereby obligates and binds itself to assume criminal and civil jurisdiction over Indians and Indian territory, country, and lands or any portion thereof within this state in accordance with the consent of the United States given by the Act of Congress of April 11, 1968, 82 Stat. 78-80 (Public Law 284, 90th Congress), to the extent authorized by that act and this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-202 Special elections on acceptance or retrocession of state jurisdiction.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-202(1): State jurisdiction acquired or retroceded pursuant to this chapter with respect to criminal offenses or civil causes of action shall be applicable in Indian country only where the enrolled Indians residing within the affected area of the Indian country accept state jurisdiction or request its retrocession by a majority vote of the adult Indians voting at a special election held for that purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-202(2): These special elections shall be called pursuant to federal law.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-203 Acceptance or rejection of cession of state jurisdiction -- Proclamation by governor.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-203(1): If the governor receives a resolution signed by the majority of any tribe, tribal council, or other governing body duly recognized by the Bureau of Indian Affairs of any tribe, community, band or group in the state certifying the results of a special election expressly ceding criminal or civil jurisdiction of the Indian tribe, community, band, or group or its lands or any portion thereof to the state of Utah within the limits authorized by federal law, he shall either accept or reject the cession of jurisdiction within 60 days.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-203(2): If the governor accepts jurisdiction, he shall issue a proclamation within 60 days to the effect that civil or criminal jurisdiction shall apply, subject to the limitations of this chapter, to all Indians and all Indian territory, country, lands or any portion thereof of the Indian body involved to the extent authorized by the resolution.  Failure to issue the proclamation within the time prescribed is considered a rejection of the assumption of jurisdiction.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-204 Criminal jurisdiction.
----------------------------------------------------
The state of Utah shall assume jurisdiction over offenses as set forth in this chapter, committed by or against Indians in the lands described in each tribal resolution 60 days after issuance of the governor's proclamation to the same extent it has jurisdiction over offenses committed elsewhere within the state.  The criminal laws of the state shall have the same force and effect within these lands as they have elsewhere within the state.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-205 Civil jurisdiction.
-------------------------------------------------
The state of Utah shall assume jurisdiction over civil causes of action as set forth in this chapter, between Indians or to which Indians are parties in the lands described in each tribal resolution 60 days after issuance of the governor's proclamation to the same extent it has jurisdiction over civil causes of action as elsewhere within the state. The civil laws of the state shall have the same force and effect within these lands as they have elsewhere within the state, except as otherwise provided by this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-206 State jurisdiction subject to provisions of federal law and resolution of tribe.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The jurisdiction assumed pursuant to this chapter is subject to the limitations and provisions of the federal Act of Congress of April 11, 1968, 82 Stat. 78-80 (Public Law 284, 90th Congress), and the specific limitations set forth in each resolution ceding jurisdiction to the state, both as to geographical area and subject matter.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-207 Retrocession of state jurisdiction -- Proclamation by governor.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-207(1): The state of Utah hereby obligates and binds itself to retrocede all or any measure of the criminal or civil jurisdiction acquired by it pursuant to this chapter whenever the governor receives a resolution from a majority of any tribe, tribal council, or other governing body duly recognized by the Bureau of Indian Affairs of any Indian tribe, community, band or group in this state, certifying the results of a special election and expressly requesting the state to retrocede jurisdiction over its people or lands or any portion thereof within the limits authorized by the Act of Congress of April 11, 1968, 82 Stat., 78-80 (Public Law 284, 90th Congress).
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-207(2): The governor shall issue within 60 days a proclamation to the effect that jurisdiction has been retroceded for all these Indians and all Indian territory, country, lands or any portion thereof.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-208 Limitations on state authority with respect to property and rights of Indians.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Nothing in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-208(1): authorizes the alienation, encumbrance, or taxation of any real or personal property, including water rights belonging to any Indian or any Indian tribe, band, or community that is held in trust by the United States or is subject to a restriction against alienation imposed by the United States;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-208(2): authorizes the regulation of the use of this property in a manner inconsistent with any federal treaty, agreement, or statute or with any regulation made pursuant to them;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-208(3): confers jurisdiction upon the state to adjudicate, in probate proceedings or otherwise, the ownership or right to possession of this property or any interest in it; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-208(4): enlarges, diminishes, or deprives any Indian or any Indian tribe, band, or community of any right, privilege, or immunity afforded under federal treaty, agreement, statute, or executive order with respect to Indian land grants, hunting, trapping, or fishing or the control, licensing, or regulation of these.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-209 Tribal ordinance or custom given full force and effect.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any tribal ordinance or custom adopted by an Indian tribe, band, or community in the exercise of any authority that it may possess shall, if not inconsistent with any applicable civil law of the state, be given full force and effect in the determination of civil causes of action.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-210 Criminal jurisdiction of state over hunting, trapping, or fishing offenses on reservations -- "Indian reservation" defined.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
As used in this part, "Indian reservation" means:Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-210(1): all land within the limits of any Indian reservation under the jurisdiction of the United States government, notwithstanding the issuance of any patent, and including rights of way running through the reservation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-210(2): all Indian allotments, to which the Indian titles have not been extinguished, including rights of way thereon.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-211 Hunting, trapping, or fishing on reservation a misdemeanor.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any person who, without lawful authority or permission from constituted tribal authorities, willfully and knowingly goes upon any real property within an Indian reservation belonging to any Indian, or any Indian tribe, band, or community, that is held in trust by the United States or is subject to a restriction against alienation imposed by the United States, for the purpose of hunting, trapping, or fishing thereon, or for the removal of game, peltries, or fish therefrom, is guilty of a class B misdemeanor, and all game, fish, and peltries in the person's possession shall be forfeited to the tribe.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-212 Jurisdiction of tribe over hunting, trapping, or fishing offenses by member.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter does not extend to offenses committed by an enrolled member of a federally recognized Indian tribe who is subject to the law of the tribe having jurisdiction of the Indian reservation, or in any case where the exclusive jurisdiction over the offense is, or may be, secured to the Indian tribes respectively.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-213 Concurrent state and federal jurisdiction over hunting, trapping, or fishing offenses on reservations.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-213(1): With respect to any of the offenses enumerated in this chapter, over which federal courts may have lawful jurisdiction, the jurisdiction of the courts of the state of Utah shall be concurrent and not exclusive.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-213(2): It shall be the duty of the courts of the state of Utah to order delivery to the proper authorities of the federal government for prosecution, any offender, there to be dealt with according to law or regulations authorized by law, where such authorities consent to exercise jurisdiction lawfully vested in them over the said offender.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214 Law enforcement in presidential townsites.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(1)(a): "Agents of the Bureau of Indian Affairs" means individuals the Bureau of Indian Affairs has empowered to enforce federal statutes in Indian land under 25 U.S.C. Sec. 2802 or 25 U.S.C. Sec. 2804.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(1)(b): "Bureau of Indian Affairs" means the Bureau of Indian Affairs within the United States Department of the Interior.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(1)(c): "Indian land" means land that qualifies as "Indian country" under 18 U.S.C. Sec. 1151.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(1)(d): "Indian tribe" or "tribe" means an Indian tribe included in the list of federally recognized Indian tribes under 25 U.S.C. Sec. 5131.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(1)(e): "Non-Indian land" means land that does not qualify as "Indian country" under 18 U.S.C. Sec. 1151.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(1)(f): "Presidential townsite with Indian land" means a municipality incorporated under the laws of the state:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(1)(f)(i): created by presidential proclamation pursuant to Sections 2380 and 2381 of the Revised Statutes of the United States, Act of Congress of March 3, 1863, 12 Stat. 754; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(1)(f)(ii): encompassing Indian land and non-Indian land within its municipal boundaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(2): A presidential townsite with Indian land may enter into an agreement that grants authority to agents of the Bureau of Indian Affairs to enforce all applicable state and local misdemeanor and felony offenses on all lands within the presidential townsite with Indian land, provided that each of the following shall be party to the agreement:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(2)(a): the presidential townsite with Indian land;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(2)(b): the local county sheriff;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(2)(c): the Indian tribe with jurisdiction over Indian lands within the presidential townsite with Indian land; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(2)(d): the Bureau of Indian Affairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(3): (2) An agreement entered into under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-214(4): (2); 53-6-103 Agents of the Bureau of Indian Affairs who are granted authority to enforce state and local criminal misdemeanor offenses and felonies under an agreement entered into under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-401 Short title.
------------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Native American Grave Protection and Repatriation Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(1): "Antiquities Section" means the Antiquities Section of the State Historic Preservation Office.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(2): "Burial site" means a natural or prepared physical location, whether originally below, on, or above the surface of the earth, into which as a part of the death rite or ceremony of a culture individual human remains are deposited.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(3): "Cultural affiliation" means that there is a relationship of shared group identity that can be reasonably traced historically or prehistorically between a present day Indian tribe and an identifiable earlier group.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(4): "Director" means the director of the Division of Indian Affairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(5): "Division" means the Division of Indian Affairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(6): "Indian tribe" means a tribe, band, nation, or other organized group or community of Indians that is recognized as eligible for the special programs and services provided by the United States to Indians because of their status as Indians.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(7): "Lineal descendant" means the genealogical descendant established by oral or written record.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(8): "Native American" means of or relating to a tribe, people, or culture that is indigenous to the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(9): "Native American remains" means remains that are Native American.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(10): 53C-1-103
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(10)(a): "Nonfederal land" means land in the state that is not owned, controlled, or held in trust by the federal government.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(10)(b): 53C-1-103 "Nonfederal land" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(10)(b)(i): land owned or controlled by:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(10)(b)(i)(A): the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(10)(b)(i)(B): a county, city, or town;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(10)(b)(i)(C): an Indian tribe, if the land is not held in trust by the United States for the Indian tribe or the Indian tribe's members; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(10)(b)(i)(D): a person other than the federal government; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(10)(b)(ii): 53C-1-103 school and institutional trust lands as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(11): "Partner agency" means an agency of the state or a tribal agency that participates in the remains repatriation process.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(12): "Remains" means all or part of a physical individual and objects on or attached to the physical individual that are placed there as part of the death rite or ceremony of a culture.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(13): 9-9-405 "Review committee" means the Native American Remains Review Committee created by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(14): 53B-3-102; 53C-1-103
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(14)(a): 53B-3-102 "State land" means land owned by the state including the state's:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(14)(a)(i): legislative and judicial branches;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(14)(a)(ii): departments, divisions, agencies, boards, commissions, councils, and committees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(14)(a)(iii): 53B-3-102 institutions of higher education as defined under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(14)(b): 53C-1-103 "State land" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(14)(b)(i): land owned by a political subdivision of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(14)(b)(ii): land owned by a school district;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(14)(b)(iii): private land; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(14)(b)(iv): 53C-1-103 school and institutional trust lands as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(15): "Tribal consultation" means the state and the tribes exchanging views and information, in writing or in person, regarding implementing proposed state action under this part that has or may have substantial implications for tribes including impacts on:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(15)(a): tribal cultural practices;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(15)(b): tribal lands;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(15)(c): tribal resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(15)(d): access to traditional areas of tribal cultural or religious importance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-402(15)(e): the consideration of the state's responsibilities to Indian tribes.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403 Ownership and disposition of Native American remains.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1): If Native American remains are discovered on nonfederal lands on or after April 30, 2007, the ownership or control of the Native American remains shall be determined in the following priority:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(a): first, in the lineal descendants of the Native American;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(b): second, if the lineal descendants cannot be ascertained, in the Indian tribe that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(b)(i): has the closest cultural affiliation with the Native American remains; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(b)(ii): states a claim for the Native American remains; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(c): third:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(c)(i): in the Indian tribe that is recognized as aboriginally occupying the area in which the Native American remains are discovered, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(c)(i)(A): cultural affiliation of the Native American remains cannot be reasonably ascertained;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(c)(i)(B): the land is recognized either by a final judgment of the Indian Claims Commission or through other evidence as the exclusive or joint aboriginal land of some Indian tribe; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(c)(i)(C): that tribe states a claim for the Native American remains; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(c)(ii): in a different tribe if:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(c)(ii)(A): it can be shown by a preponderance of the evidence that that different tribe has a stronger genetic or cultural relationship with the Native American remains; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-403(1)(c)(ii)(B): that different tribe states a claim for the Native American remains.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-404 Illegal trafficking.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-404(1): Any person who knowingly sells, purchases, uses for profit, or transports for sale or profit the remains of a Native American without the right of possession to those remains as provided in this part is guilty of a class A misdemeanor.  In the case of a second or subsequent violation the person is guilty of a third degree felony.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-404(2): Any person who knowingly sells, purchases, exchanges, receives, uses for profit, or transports for sale or profit any Native American remains obtained in violation of this part is guilty of a class A misdemeanor.  In the case of a second or subsequent violation the person is guilty of a third degree felony.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-406 Savings provision.
------------------------------------------------
Nothing in this part may be construed to:Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-406(1): limit the authority of a state agency to:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-406(1)(a): return or repatriate Native American remains to Indian tribes or individuals; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-406(1)(b): enter into another agreement with the consent of the lineal descendant or culturally affiliated tribe as to the disposition or control over Native American remains;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-406(2): delay actions on repatriation requests that are pending on March 17, 1992;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-406(3): 9-9-403(6) deny or otherwise affect access to any court, except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-406(4): limit any procedural or substantive rights that may otherwise be secured to individuals or Indian tribes; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-406(5): limit the application of any state or federal law pertaining to theft or stolen property.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408 Burial of ancient Native American remains in state parks.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(1): 9-8a-302; 9-9-402; 9-8a-304 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(1)(a): 9-8a-302; 9-9-402 "Ancient Native American remains" means ancient human remains, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(1)(b): 9-8a-304 "Antiquities Section" means the Antiquities Section of the State Historic Preservation Office created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(2)(a): The division, the Antiquities Section, and the Division of State Parks shall cooperate in a study of the feasibility of burying ancient Native American remains in state parks.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(2)(b): The study shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(2)(b)(i): the process and criteria for determining which state parks would have land sufficient and appropriate to reserve a portion of the land for the burial of ancient Native American remains;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(2)(b)(ii): the process for burying the ancient Native American remains on the lands within state parks, including the responsibilities of state agencies and the assurance of cultural sensitivity;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(2)(b)(iii): how to keep a record of the locations in which specific ancient Native American remains are buried;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(2)(b)(iv): how to account for the costs of:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(2)(b)(iv)(A): burying the ancient Native American remains on lands found within state parks; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(2)(b)(iv)(B): securing and maintaining burial sites in state parks; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-9-408(2)(b)(v): any issues related to burying ancient Native American remains in state parks.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 9 - Chapter 20 - Utah Commission on Service and Volunteerism Act
********************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Utah Commission on Service and Volunteerism Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-102(1): "Act" means the National Community and Service Trust Act of 1993, 42 U.S.C. 12501 et seq.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-102(2): 9-20-201 "Commission" means the Utah Commission on Service and Volunteerism created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-102(3): "Corporation" means the Corporation for National and Community Service described in the act.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201 Creation -- Members -- Appointment -- Terms -- Vacancies -- Per diem and expenses.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(1): There is created the Utah Commission on Service and Volunteerism consisting of 19 voting members and one nonvoting member.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2): The 19 voting members of the commission are:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(a): the lieutenant governor;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(b): the commissioner of higher education or the commissioner's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(c): the state superintendent of public instruction or the superintendent's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(d): the executive director of the Department of Cultural and Community Engagement or the executive director's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(e): nine members appointed by the governor as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(e)(i): an individual with expertise in the educational, training, and developmental needs of youth, particularly disadvantaged youth;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(e)(ii): an individual with experience in promoting the involvement of older adults in volunteer service;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(e)(iii): a representative of a community-based agency or organization within the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(e)(iv): a representative of local government;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(e)(v): a representative of a local labor organization in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(e)(vi): a representative of business;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(e)(vii): an individual between the ages of 16 and 25 who participates in a volunteer or service program;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(e)(viii): a representative of a national service program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(e)(ix): a representative of the volunteer sector; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(f): six members appointed by the governor from among the following groups:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(f)(i): local educators;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(f)(ii): experts in the delivery of human, educational, cultural, environmental, or public safety services to communities and individuals;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(f)(iii): representatives of Native American tribes;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(f)(iv): representatives of organizations that assist out-of-school youth or other at-risk youth; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(2)(f)(v): representatives of entities that receive assistance under the Domestic Volunteer Service Act of 1973, 42 U.S.C. 4950 et seq.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(3): The nonvoting member of the commission is the regional representative of the corporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(4)(a): In appointing persons to serve on the commission, the governor shall ensure that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(4)(a)(i): no more than 10 voting members of the commission are members of the same political party; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(4)(a)(ii): no more than five voting members of the commission are state government employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(4)(b): In appointing persons to serve on the commission, the governor shall strive for balance on the commission according to race, ethnicity, age, gender, disability characteristics, and geography.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(5)(a): Except as required by Subsection (5)(b), as terms of current commission members expire, the governor shall appoint each new member or reappointed member to a three-year term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(5)(b): Notwithstanding the requirements of Subsection (5)(a), the governor shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of terms to ensure that the terms of commission members are staggered so that approximately one-third of the commission is appointed every year.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(6): When a vacancy occurs in the membership, the replacement shall be appointed for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(7): A member appointed by the governor may not serve more than two consecutive terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(8): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(8)(a): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(8)(b): 63A-3-107 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-201(8)(c): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance pursuant to Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-202 Election of commission chair and vice chair.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-202(1): The chair as of May 1, 2024, remains the chair until the completion of the chair's current term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-202(2): Subject to Subsection (3), the voting members of the commission shall elect a vice chair from among the voting members of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-202(3): The voting members of the commission may not elect the lieutenant governor as vice chair of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-202(4): The chair and vice chair shall serve for a term of one year.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-202(5): The chair becomes the past chair after the chair completes the one-year term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-202(6): The vice chair becomes the chair after the vice chair completes the one-year term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-202(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-202(7)(a): Subject to Subsection (7)(b), if for any reason the chair does not complete a one-year term, the voting members of the commission shall elect a chair from among the voting members of the commission to complete the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-202(7)(b): The voting members of the commission may not elect the lieutenant governor as the chair of the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-203 Commission chair and vice chair duties.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-203(1): The chair shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-203(1)(a): preside at meetings of the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-203(1)(b): authorize and execute the actions of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-203(2): The vice chair shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-203(2)(a): assist the chair;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-203(2)(b): if the chair is absent, perform the duties of the chair;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-203(2)(c): accept special assignments from the chair; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-203(2)(d): perform other duties as delegated by the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-204 Meetings -- Quorum.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-204(1): The commission shall meet at least four times each year at the call of the chair.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-204(2): A commission quorum is a simple majority of the voting members.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-205 Commission duties.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-205(1): 9-20-301 The commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-205(1)(a): administer the selection, development, and oversight of programs funded and established by the act;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-205(1)(b): pursue opportunities for sustainable and high-impact community service;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-205(1)(c): develop and annually update a three-year state service plan, including the establishment of state priorities;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-205(1)(d): 9-20-301 provide policy guidance to the One Utah Service Fellowship Program described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-205(1)(e): stimulate increased community awareness of the impact of volunteer service in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-205(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-205(2)(a): The commission may, subject to Title 63J, Chapter 5, Federal Funds Procedures Act, receive and accept federal funds, and may receive and accept private gifts, donations, or funds from any source.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-205(2)(b): Money received under this Subsection (2) shall be deposited with the state and shall be available to the commission to carry out the purposes of this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-206 Reporting and administration.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-206(1): The executive director of the department, in consultation with the commission, shall appoint a director of the commission who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-206(1)(a): experienced in administration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-206(1)(b): qualified by education or training in the field of public administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-206(2): The director of the commission shall report to the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-206(3): The commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-206(3)(a): report to the office of the lieutenant governor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-206(3)(b): by January 1, provide an annual written report to the lieutenant governor on service and volunteerism in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-206(4): The department shall provide administrative and staff support services to the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-207 Rulemaking.
------------------------------------------
In accordance withUtah Code Annotated § 9-20-207(1): implement this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-207(2): ensure the commission complies with the act and related federal requirements.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301 One Utah Service Fellowship Program.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1): 53B-2-101 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(a): "Education expense" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(a)(i): tuition or student fees at an institution of higher education that participates in the federal student assistance programs under the Higher Education Act of 1965, Title IV, 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1070 et seq.;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(a)(ii): repayment of a student loan; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(a)(iii): other costs of attending an institution of higher education described in Subsection (1)(a)(i), as determined by the institution of higher education, for a degree or certificate program, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(a)(iii)(A): books;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(a)(iii)(B): supplies;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(a)(iii)(C): transportation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(a)(iii)(D): room and board.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(b): "Eligible recipient" means an individual who:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(b)(i): is a resident of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(b)(ii): successfully completes a fellowship under the program created in this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(b)(iii): is a citizen of the United States, a United States national, or a lawful permanent resident of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(c): "Federal requirements for the AmeriCorps program" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(c)(i): relevant provisions of:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(c)(i)(A): the National and Community Service Act of 1990, as amended, 42 U.S.C. 12501 et seq. and corresponding federal regulations;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(c)(i)(B): the Domestic Volunteer Service Act of 1973, as amended, 42 U.S.C. 4950 et seq. and corresponding federal regulations;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(c)(i)(C): the Federal Grant and Cooperative Agreement Act, as amended, 31 U.S.C. Secs. 6301 through 6308, and corresponding federal regulations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(c)(i)(D): AmeriCorps' C.F.R. Chapters XII and XXV; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(c)(ii): any terms and conditions associated with AmeriCorps federal grant funding.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(d): 53B-2-101 "Institution of higher education" means an entity described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(e): "Participant" means an individual who:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(e)(i): is at least 17 years old;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(e)(ii): has received a high school diploma or its equivalent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(e)(iii): the program matches with a qualified partner organization to participate in a program fellowship.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(f): "Program" means the One Utah Service Fellowship Program created in Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(g): "Qualified partner organization" means a nonprofit organization or government entity that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(g)(i): agrees to supervise a participant for the total number of hours outlined in an agreement with the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(g)(ii): except as provided in Subsection (4)(d), agrees to provide the commission with a matching stipend amount, as described in Subsection (5); and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(g)(iii): provides a valuable service to the community, as determined by the commission or commission rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(h): "Supervise" means the act of overseeing the work of an eligible recipient, including some component of in-person interaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(i): "Third-party administrator" means an entity that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(i)(i): enters into an agreement with the department, as described in Subsection (7);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(i)(ii): is a nonprofit organization or subsidiary or affiliate of an institution of higher education;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(i)(iii): has experience managing programs and funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(i)(iv): operates under the direction of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(1)(j): "Tuition award" means an amount of money to be used for an education expense, as described in Subsection (6).
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(2): There is created a One Utah Service Fellowship Program to provide meaningful service opportunities to young adults in the state to:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(2)(a): prepare young adults for additional educational, training, and career opportunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(2)(b): address high-priority needs within the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(2)(c): provide a stipend to a participant and a tuition award to an eligible recipient in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(a): Subject to appropriations from the Legislature, the commission shall administer the program as described in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b): Except as otherwise provided in an agreement authorized by Subsection (7)(b), the commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(i): shall create and maintain a list of high-priority policy needs in the state where program service opportunities can provide the most value to the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(ii): shall receive an application from a potential participant;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(iii): shall match a participant to a qualified partner organization for participation in the program;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(iv): shall approve a potential qualified partner organization to participate in the program;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(v): shall prioritize the placement of participants with qualified partner organizations that address the high-priority policy needs identified under Subsection (3)(b)(i);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(vi): shall create and maintain, or contract with a third-party to create and maintain, an online portal that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(vi)(A): provides information about the program, including required qualifications for participation, tuition awards, and stipends;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(vi)(B): lists all service opportunities with qualified partner organizations that are available through the program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(vi)(C): allows a potential participant to apply for placement with a qualified partner organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(vii): shall determine the metrics of success of the program, including metrics regarding whether an eligible recipient:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(vii)(A): matriculates at an institution of higher education after completing a One Utah Service Fellowship; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(vii)(B): graduates from, or otherwise completes a program at, an institution of higher education;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(viii): shall measure the success of the program according to the metrics determined under this Subsection (3);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(ix): shall coordinate with institutions of higher education to:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(ix)(A): connect an eligible recipient with additional educational, training, certification, and apprenticeship opportunities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(ix)(B): explore options to award an eligible recipient with academic credit for the completion of a One Utah Service Fellowship, in addition to the stipend and tuition award;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(x): may solicit private donations to supplement the program, including to offset a matching amount required of a qualified partner organization as described in Subsection (4)(d);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(xi): shall market and provide outreach for the program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(b)(xii): shall ensure the program complies with federal requirements for the AmeriCorps program administered by the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(3)(c): The commission may make rules in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, to implement this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(a): Before a participant begins providing service through the program, the commission or third-party administrator shall enter into an agreement with the participant that outlines the mutual expectations of the program and the participant.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(b): The agreement described in Subsection (4)(a) shall detail the requirements of the participant, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(b)(i): the total number of hours of service required under the agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(b)(ii): the exact stipend amount promised to the participant in consideration of service, as described in Subsection (5);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(b)(iii): the exact tuition award amount promised to the participant upon successful completion of a fellowship, as described in Subsection (6);
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(b)(iv): qualifications for and acceptable uses of the tuition award, as described in Subsection (6); and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(b)(v): the circumstances under which the agreement may be amended, including for participant hardship or compelling personal circumstance.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(c)(i): Subject to Subsection (4)(c)(ii), before a qualified partner organization accepts service from a participant, the commission or third-party administrator shall enter into an agreement with the qualified partner organization that outlines the mutual expectations of the program and qualified partner organization, including the exact amount of matching funds the qualified partner organization shall provide to the commission to contribute to a participant's stipend.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(c)(ii): A qualified partner organization shall agree to contribute no less than $5 per hour to a participant's stipend.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(4)(d): The agreement described in Subsection (4)(c) may include a provision that the program is reducing the qualified partner organization's matching fund requirement due to the receipt of private donations, as described in Subsection (5)(c)(ii)(B).
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(a): The commission may issue, and a participant may receive, a stipend for participating in the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(b): The commission or third-party administrator shall establish the exact stipend for a participant on a case-by-case basis in an agreement described in Subsection (4)(a) based on:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(b)(i): available program funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(b)(ii): any matching funds provided by:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(b)(ii)(A): the qualified partner organization with which the participant is paired; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(b)(ii)(B): private donations to the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(c)(i): The commission or third-party administrator shall contribute $5 per hour of the stipend described in this Subsection (5), up to $8,500 for the term of the agreement, from state funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(c)(ii): The commission or third-party administrator shall supplement the remaining balance of a participant's exact stipend from non-state funds, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(c)(ii)(A): matching funds provided to the commission by a qualified partner organization; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(c)(ii)(B): private donations to the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(c)(iii): The commission or third-party administrator shall prioritize a participant's placement with a qualified partner organization based on the amount of matching funds the qualified partner organization proposes to provide to the commission under Subsection (5)(c)(ii)(A), with preference going to qualified partner organizations that offer to provide a larger stipend.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(5)(c)(iv): The commission or third-party administrator shall disburse the stipend to a participant in installments, no less frequently than every three months.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(a): The commission shall provide a tuition award to an eligible recipient, according to the terms of the agreement described in Subsection (4), upon the successful completion of a fellowship.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(b): The commission or third-party administrator shall establish the exact tuition award for an eligible recipient on a case-by-case basis in an agreement described in Subsection (4)(a) based on:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(b)(i): federal requirements for the AmeriCorps program, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(b)(i)(A): a maximum tuition award for 1,700 hours of service during a one-year period; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(b)(i)(B): a reduced tuition award for a reduced number of hours of service during a one-year period.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(c): An eligible recipient may use a tuition award:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(c)(i): for an eligible education expense;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(c)(ii): over a seven-year period beginning the day on which the eligible recipient receives the tuition award; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(c)(iii): subject to the requirements of Subsection (6)(d).
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(d): If the program uses state funds to supplement a tuition award:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(d)(i): the commission or third-party administrator shall detail that information in an agreement described in Subsection (4)(a); and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(6)(d)(ii): an eligible recipient may only use the state funded portion of the tuition award after the eligible recipient has exhausted any scholarship, education grant, or financial aid.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(7): The department:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(7)(a): shall provide staff support to the commission to implement the program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-20-301(7)(b): may enter into an agreement with one or more third-party administrators to administer and implement the program under the direction of the commission, including by fulfilling one or more of the responsibilities described in Subsection (3).


Utah Code Annotated - Title 9 - Chapter 21 - Division of Multicultural Affairs Act
**********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Division of Multicultural Affairs Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-102(1): 9-21-301 "Commission" means the Utah Multicultural Commission created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-102(2): "Director" means the director of the Division of Multicultural Affairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-102(3): 9-21-201 "Division" means the Division of Multicultural Affairs created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-102(4): 9-21-401 "Human rights commission" means the Utah Martin Luther King, Jr. Human Rights Commission created in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-201 Creation.
----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-201(1): There is created within the department the Division of Multicultural Affairs under the administration and general supervision of the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-201(2): The division shall be under the policy direction of the executive director in consultation with the director and the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-202 Responsibilities of the division.
----------------------------------------------------------------
The responsibilities of the division include:Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-202(1): identifying the needs of the state's multicultural communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-202(2): promoting inclusiveness and cultivating trust and cooperation between the state, nonprofit entities receiving state funds, and the state's multicultural communities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-202(3): working with state agencies to ensure the state provides equitable resources, services, and programs to address the needs of the state's multicultural communities.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-203 Reporting requirements.
------------------------------------------------------
The division shall submit an annual written report to the department for inclusion in the department's annual report described in SectionUtah Code Annotated § 9-21-203(1): the division in meeting the division's responsibilities as described in this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-203(2): 9-21-302 the commission in meeting the commission's responsibilities as described in this chapter, including the strategic plan described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-203(3): the human rights commission in meeting the human rights commission's responsibilities as described in this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301 Creation of commission -- Membership -- Rulemaking.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(1): There is created within the division the Utah Multicultural Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(2): The commission shall consist of the following 13 members, appointed by the governor:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(2)(a): one individual who advises the governor on education issues;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(2)(b): one individual who advises the governor on homelessness issues;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(2)(c): one individual who advises the governor on legislative policy;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(2)(d): one individual who advises the governor on criminal and juvenile justice issues;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(2)(e): one individual who advises the governor on issues concerning families and children; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(2)(f): eight individuals who represent Utah's multicultural communities.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(3): (3)(a)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(3)(a): A member of the commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(3)(a)(i): shall serve for a term of two years; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(3)(a)(ii): may not serve more than two terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(3)(b): (3)(a)(i) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(3)(c): When a vacancy occurs in the membership, the governor shall appoint a replacement for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(4): A majority of the members of the commission constitutes a quorum of the commission at any meeting, and the action of the majority of members present is the action of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(5): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(5)(a): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(5)(b): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance pursuant to Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(6): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The department shall make rules establishing the membership, duties, and procedures of the commission in accordance with the requirements of:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(6)(a): this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(6)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-301(7): The department shall provide administrative support to the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302 Commission duties.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(1): (1)(b)(i) The commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(1)(a): cooperate with the division and state agencies to ensure the state's resources, services, and programs:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(1)(a)(i): advance the interests of the state's multicultural communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(1)(a)(ii): are properly communicated and delivered to the state's multicultural communities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(1)(a)(iii): promote a climate of inclusion in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(1)(b): (1)(b)(i) develop and submit to the lieutenant governor an annual report that includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(1)(b)(i): a description of the needs, goals, and deliverables that will directly impact the most significant and urgent needs of the state's multicultural communities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(1)(b)(ii): (1)(b)(i) recommendations on how the state should act to address the needs, goals, and deliverables described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(1)(c): convene an annual meeting to discuss issues affecting the state's multicultural communities in coordination with the governor, lieutenant governor, and relevant stakeholders.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(2): (1) In carrying out the duties described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(2)(a): consult with the lieutenant governor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(2)(b): prioritize programs and efforts related to:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(2)(b)(i): employment;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(2)(b)(ii): education;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(2)(b)(iii): housing;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(2)(b)(iv): criminal and juvenile justice; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-302(2)(b)(v): health and mental health, including suicide prevention.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401 Creation of human rights commission -- Membership -- Rulemaking.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(1): There is created within the division the Utah Martin Luther King, Jr. Human Rights Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(2)(a): The human rights commission shall consist of 13 members appointed by the governor to two-year terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(2)(b): (2)(a) Notwithstanding the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(3): The governor shall appoint one of the members as chair of the human rights commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(4): The human rights commission shall meet at least quarterly.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(5): A majority of the members of the human rights commission constitutes a quorum of the human rights commission at any meeting, and the action of the majority of members present is the action of the human rights commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(6): A member appointed by the governor may not serve more than two consecutive terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(7): When a vacancy occurs in the membership, the governor shall appoint a replacement for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(8): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(8)(a): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(8)(b): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance pursuant to Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(9): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The department shall make rules establishing the membership, duties, and procedures of the human rights commission in accordance with the requirements of:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(9)(a): this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(9)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-401(10): The department shall provide administrative support to the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-402 Human rights commission duties.
--------------------------------------------------------------
The human rights commission shall:Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-402(1): promote Dr. Martin Luther King, Jr. Day by:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-402(1)(a): encouraging appropriate ceremonies and activities commemorating the federal and state holiday, which occurs on the third Monday of January each year;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-402(1)(b): seeking to involve the public and private sectors in promoting diversity, equality, and human rights;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-402(1)(c): providing recommendations and assistance to government entities and private organizations regarding the observance of the holiday;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-402(1)(d): coordinating efforts with state residents of diverse backgrounds and with private organizations regarding the observance of the holiday; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-402(1)(e): partnering with educational institutions to assist schools in promoting appropriate events to honor human rights and the holiday; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-21-402(2): report annually to the division regarding the activities of the commission.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 9 - Chapter 22 - Stem Action Center
***************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "STEM Action Center."

Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(1): "Computing partnerships" means a set of skills, knowledge, and aptitudes used in computer science, information technology, or computer engineering courses and career options.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(2): "Director" means the director appointed by the STEM board to oversee the administration of the STEM Action Center.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(3): 53E-6-102 "Educator" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(4): 9-22-104(3); (4) "Foundation" means a foundation established as described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(5): 9-22-105 "Fund" means the STEM Action Center Foundation Fund created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(6): "Grant program" means the Computing Partnerships Grants program created in this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(7): "High quality professional development" means professional development that meets high quality standards developed by the State Board of Education.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(8): 53B-1-102 "Institution of higher education" means an institution listed in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(9): "K-16" means kindergarten through grade 12 and post-secondary education programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(10): 9-22-107 "Provider" means a provider selected on behalf of the STEM board by the staff of the STEM board and the staff of the State Board of Education:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(10)(a): through a request for proposals process; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(10)(b): 9-22-107 through a direct award or sole source procurement process for a pilot described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(11): 9-22-114 "Review committee" means the committee established under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(12): "Stacked credentials" means credentials that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(12)(a): an individual can build upon to access an advanced job or higher wage;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(12)(b): are part of a career pathway system;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(12)(c): provide a pathway culminating in the equivalent of an associate's or bachelor's degree;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(12)(d): facilitate multiple exit and entry points; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(12)(e): recognize sub-goals or momentum points.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(13): "STEM" means science, technology, engineering, and mathematics.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(14): 9-22-106 "STEM Action Center" means the center described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(15): 9-22-103 "STEM board" means the STEM Action Center Board created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-102(16): 53B-34-103 "Talent Ready Program" means the Talent Ready Utah Program created in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103 STEM Action Center Board creation -- Membership.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(1): There is created the STEM Action Center Board, composed of the following members:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(1)(a): seven private sector members who represent business, appointed by the governor;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(1)(b): the state superintendent of public instruction or the state superintendent's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(1)(c): the commissioner of higher education or the commissioner's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(1)(d): one member appointed by the governor;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(1)(e): a member of the State Board of Education, chosen by the chair of the State Board of Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(1)(f): the executive director of the department or the executive director's designee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(1)(g): the executive director of the Department of Workforce Services or the executive director's designee.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(2): (1)(a); (2)(c)
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(2)(a): (1)(a) The private sector members appointed by the governor in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(2)(b): (2)(c) Except as required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(2)(c): The length of terms of the members shall be staggered so that approximately half of the committee is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(2)(d): The members may not serve more than two full consecutive terms except where the governor determines that an additional term is in the best interest of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(2)(e): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the replacement shall be appointed for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(3): Attendance of a simple majority of the members constitutes a quorum for the transaction of official committee business.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(4): Formal action by the STEM board requires a majority vote of a quorum.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(5): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(5)(a): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(5)(b): 63A-3-107 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(5)(c): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(6): The governor shall select the chair of the STEM board to serve a two-year term.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-103(7): The executive director of the department or the executive director's designee shall serve as the vice chair of the STEM board.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-106(2)(k)(ii): how many individuals are using the data, including the demographics of the users, if available;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-106(2)(l): as appropriate, join and participate in a national STEM network;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-106(2)(m): work cooperatively with the State Board of Education to designate schools as STEM schools, where the schools have agreed to adopt a plan of STEM implementation in alignment with criteria set by the State Board of Education and the  board;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-106(2)(n): support best methods of high quality professional development for STEM education in kindergarten through grade 12, including methods of high quality professional development that reduce cost and increase effectiveness, to help educators learn how to most effectively implement best practice learning tools in classrooms;

Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-107(3)(a)(ii): grades 7 and 8; or

Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-110(2): (1) The high quality professional development application described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-110(2)(b): allow educators to access automatic tools, resources, and strategies , including instructional materials with integrated STEM content;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-110(2)(c): allow educators to work in online learning communities, including giving and receiving feedback via uploaded video;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-110(2)(d): track and report data on the usage of the components of the application's system and the relationship to improvement in classroom instruction;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-110(2)(e): include video examples of highly effective STEM education teaching that:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-110(2)(e)(i): cover a cross section of grade levels and subjects;

Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-110(2)(f): allow for additional STEM education video content to be added.

Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112 High school STEM education initiative.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(1): Subject to legislative appropriations, after consulting with State Board of Education staff, the STEM Action Center shall award grants to school districts and charter schools to fund STEM related certification for high school students.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(2)(a): A school district or charter school may apply for a grant from the STEM Action Center, through a competitive process, to fund the school district's or charter school's STEM related certification training program.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(2)(b): A school district's or charter school's STEM related certification training program shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(2)(b)(i): prepare high school students to be job ready for available STEM related positions of employment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(2)(b)(ii): when a student completes the program, result in the student gaining an industry-recognized employer STEM related certification.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(3): 53B-2a-105 A school district or charter school may partner with one or more of the following to provide a STEM related certification program:
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(3)(a): 53B-2a-105 a technical college described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(3)(b): Salt Lake Community College;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(3)(c): Snow College;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(3)(d): Utah State University Eastern;
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(3)(e): Utah State University Blanding; or
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-112(3)(f): a private sector employer.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-113(1)(f): "Employer" means a private employer, public employer, industry association, union, or the military.
Utah Code Annotated § 9-22-113(1)(g): 53E-6-102 "License" means the same as that term is defined in Section
